X. Open Comments from the Public 
Kathleen McGraw via Zoom- Questioned SEQRA process in regards to Scotts Point, 
and questioned if the Town was comfortable with their decision.  
  
For more information visit our website at www.townofriverheadny.gov  
 
 
John Cullin- Spoke of public comments on social media in regards to the Science 
Center, and its possible condemnation.  
 
Ron Harari- via Zoom- Questioned the financials and ability of master developer who 
may be appointed to over see the Town Square development project.  
 
John McAuliff- Complimented the Suffolk Theatre in its production of 12 Angry Men 
play. Encouraged the Town to create renderings of the total proposed Town Square 
development.  
 
Colleen O'Brian- via Zoom- Inquired if the Riverhead IDA will be billed for their 
portion of the current litigation involving CAT and the Epcal Property. 
XI. Adjournment 
The meeting was closed at 3:20 PM 
 
 
 
 
James Wooten, Town Clerk 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
NOTICE REGARDING TOWN BOARD MEETING 
 
PLEASE TAKE NOTICE that the Town Board Meeting scheduled for April 1, 2025 at 2:00 p.m. at 
Riverhead Town Hall, 4 West Second Street, Riverhead, New York will proceed as scheduled.     
PLEASE TAKE FURTHER NOTICE , that in addition to in person atte ndance, the public can 
view the April 1, 2025 meeting of the Town Board via the following methods:  
1. Live stream; namely, by viewing it on your television on Channel 22;  
2. Logging on the Town of Riverhead website, www.townofriverheadny.gov and clicking 
on the link “Channel 22” on Quick Links on the home page or by connecting to the URL, 
which is as follows: townofriverheadny.viebit.com/player_live.php  
3.  Zoom Meeting, log in as follows: 
https://us02web.zoom.us/j/85091664603?pwd=bh1RbtnCswjx9OCKbXarria5ivQR3v.1 
 
Webinar ID: 850 9166 4603     Password:  437553          Dial by your location: (929) 205-6099 
 
PLEASE TAKE FURTHER NOTICE, that upon entering the Zoom meeting, you will be 
placed in a virtual audience. From there, you may either passively watch the public hearing 
live, or communicate to the moderator/host your request to make a comment during the 
public comment section for PUBLIC HEARINGS, RESOLUTIONS and/or OPEN 
COMMENTS. To alert the moderator/host of your desire to be heard, use the “CHAT” or 
“RAISE HAND” feature, then use the “CHAT” feature to inform the moderator/host of the 
following: 
1) Name; 2) Hamlet; 3) Public Hearing, Resolution and/or Open Comment Topic. 
 
If you are calling in, please dial *9 to “raise your hand”, so we can acknowledge your request 
to speak. 
 
When it is your turn to speak, your status will be temporarily changed so you can be unmuted 
and visible for the three-minute comment period. After three minutes, you will be placed back 
in the audience. 
 
Comments/questions will be limited to three minutes. Please be patient; your admittance will 
be based on the volume of participants. Any problems or issues getting t o the Town Board 
meeting via telephone or computer should be directed to (631) 727-3200 x655.

BUDGET ADOPTION 
 
Councilman Rothwell offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilman Kern 
 
WHEREAS, the Town Board Resolution 2022-731 established the creation of 
capital project #82222 in connection with extending the Riverhead Water District 
facilities to service the Printed Places Subdivision designated as District 0600, Section 
82, Block 1, Lot 9.8 on the Suffolk County Tax Map, and 
 
WHEREAS, the Riverhead Water District has received a check from Blue Moon 
Property Management LLC representing 20% of the estimated project costs to the 
existing project Printed Places Subdivision, Middle Rd, Riverhead, New York, and 
 
NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Supervisor is hereby authorized 
to make the following budget adjustments; 
  
 FROM  TO

04.01.2025 ADOPTED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-282 
 
RATIFIES ACCEPTANCE OF DONATION OF FLAGPOLE FROM EAST END 
EMERALD SOCIETY 
 
Councilwoman Merrifield offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilwoman Waski 
 
WHEREAS, the East End Emerald Society, P.O. Box 327, Jamesport, NY 11947 
donated a 25 foot Flag Pole to the George Young Community Center with an 
approximate value of $1,850.00 (One Thousand Eight Hundred and Fifty Dollars); and  
 
WHEREAS,  pursuant to Town Law, § 64(8), the Town Board is expressly 
authorized to accept a gift “. . . for any public use, upon such terms or conditions as may 
be prescribed by the grantor or donor and accepted by said town, and provide for the 
proper administration of the same”; and  
  
WHEREAS, the Town Board finds that acceptance of this Flag Pole at no cost to 
the Town is in the best interest of the residents of the Town of Riverhead.  
 
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED , that the Town of Riverhead hereby 
ratifies the acceptance of the donation of  a 25 foot Flag Pole for the George Young 
Community Center with an approximate value of $1,850.00 (One Thousand Eight 
Hundred and Fifty Dollars) from the East End Emerald Society; and be it further  
 
RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of 
this resolution from the electronic storage device and, if needed, a certified copy of 
same may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk.  
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Denise Merrifield, Councilwoman 
SECONDER: Joann Waski, Councilwoman 
AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

TB Resolution 2025-286 
 
APPOINTS TRAFFIC CONTROL SPECIALISTS 
 
Councilwoman Merrifield offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilwoman Waski 
 
WHEREAS, Part-time Traffic Control Specialists are needed at the Riverhead 
Police Department to direct pedestrians and vehicular traffic during special events, 
issue summonses, and enforce rules and regulations relating to the parking, standing, 
and stopping of vehicles; and  
 
WHEREAS, interviews were conducted and a recommendation of suitable 
candidates has been made by the supervising police officer.  
 
NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that effective April 1, 2025, and 
pursuant to a successfully completed background investigations, and drug and alcohol 
testing administered by the Town, this Town Board hereby appoints Nicolena Ajcuc and 
Zachariah Sapolin to the position of Part-time Traffic Control Specialist at an hourly rate 
of $21.00.  
 
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is hereby directed to forward 
a copy of this resolution to Nicolena Ajcuc, Zachariah Sapolin, the Chief of Police, the 
Personnel Officer, and the Financial Administrator. Town Hall departments may review 
and obtain a copy of this resolution from the electronic storage device.  
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Denise Merrifield, Councilwoman 
SECONDER: Joann Waski, Councilwoman 
AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

TB Resolution 2025-293 
 
RATIFIES PROMOTION OF EMPLOYEE TO PROVISIONAL TITLE OF SENIOR 
WASTEWATER TREATMENT PLANT OPERATOR 4A 
 
Councilman Rothwell offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilman Kern 
 
WHEREAS, Michael Reichel has served as Wastewater District Superintendent 
Type II  since 1990 and will retire effective March 21, 2025  at 23:59:59, creating a 
vacancy in the position which is being reclassified by Suffolk County Department of Civil 
Service as a Senior Wastewater Treatment Plant Operator 4A, as the current available 
Wastewater Superintendent titles address sewer systems at lower plant scores than 
that of the Towns; and 
 
WHEREAS, the Town desires to promote and appoint Timothy Allen  to the  
provisional title of Senior Wastewater Treatment Plant Operator 4A, which will be 
internally designated as Wastewater District Superintendent effective March 22, 2025 at 
00:00:00 based upon Timothy Allen’s lengthy service and commitment to the Town of 
Riverhead, experience, qualifying license from the State of New York  Department of 
Environmental Conservation, and in furtherance of administrative stability and continuity 
within the Riverhead Sewer District; and  
 
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED , that the To wn Board of the Town of 
Riverhead does hereby ratify the promotion of Timothy Allen from Senior Wastewater 
Treatment Plant Operator 3A also individually designated as the Wastewater District 
Deputy Superintendent  to the provisional title of Senior Wastewat er Treatment Plant 
Operator 4A of the Riverhead Sewer District, which shall be internally designated as the 
Wastewater District Superintendent  effective March 22, 2025  at 00:00:00; and be it 
further, 
 
RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk be and is hereby authoriz ed to forward a copy 
of this resolution to the Riverhead Sewer District , Timothy Allen , and the Accounting 
Department; and be it further,  
 
RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of 
this resolution from the electronic storage  device and, if needed, a certified copy of 
same may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk.   
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Kenneth Rothwell, Councilman 
SECONDER: Robert Kern, Councilman 
AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

9.15
Packet Pg. 108
 
Agreement made and entered into this  _____ day of March, 2025 between THE 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD, County of Suffolk, and State of New York, hereinafter referred to 
as the “Town”, and Tim Allen, serving as the Sewer District Superintendent for the Town of 
Riverhead, New York, hereinafter referred to as “employee” or “Allen”.   
 
W I T N E S S E T H: 
 
WHEREAS, the Town desires to provide Allen in his capacity as the Sewer District 
Superintendent with written terms and conditions of employment in ord er to enhance 
administrative stability and continuity within the Town, which the Town believes generally 
improves the quality of its overall mission; and 
 
WHEREAS, pursuant to County of Suffolk Department of Human Resources, 
Personnel & Civil Service a revised duty statement for his provisional appointment to Senior 
Wastewater Plant Operator 4/A, provisional pending meeting requirements for promotional 
to such title, which describes his position and role as the Sewer District Superintendent of 
the Town of Riverhead has been approved; and 
 
WHEREAS, the Town and  Allen believe that written term s and conditions of 
employment are necessary to describe specifically their relationship and to serve as the 
basis of effective communication betwe en them a s they fulfill their governanc e and 
administrative functions in the operation of the Town; and 
 
WHEREAS, this Agreement supersedes all prior agreements between the parties; 
and 
 
WHEREAS, this Agreement cannot be, in whole or in part, amended orally by the 
parties. 
 
NOW THEREFORE, in exchange of the mutual covenants and considerations, it is 
agreed that the terms and conditions of employment of Allen while employed as the Sewer 
District Superintendent of the Town of Riverhead shall be as follows: 
 
ARTICLE I 
DURATION 
 
 
1.  This Agreement shall be effective as of March 22, 2025 and shall continue in full 
force and effect during the period o f time Employee serves as the “Sewer District 
Superintendent”, including such period of time classified as provisional and/or probationary 
period through and including successful movement from provisional to permanent status, 
subject to any and all such rights of th e Town to modify the te rms and/or terminate 
Employee consistent with applicable provisions of this Agreement, a Collective Bargaining 
Agreement or Civil Service Laws, Rules or Regulations.  
 
 
 
9.15.a
Packet Pg. 109
Attachment: Employment Contract Tim Allen  (2025-294 : Ratifies Setting Terms and Conditions of Employment for Sewer District
 
ARTICLE II 
RECOGNITION 
 
1.  The Town recognizes Employee’s right to bargain for the terms and conditions of 
his employment with the Town.  Both parties acknowledge that this Agreement is personal 
to the Employee and shall not inure to his successor.  Such recognition is for the period of 
this Agreement or extensions hereof.  
 
2.  Employee affirms that he does not assert the right to strike against the Town, or 
to assist or participate in any such strike, picket, job action or any work slowdown. 
 
3.  The Town recognizes Employee’s right to designate a representative to appear 
on his behalf to discuss salaries, working conditions, grievances and disputes relative to 
the terms and conditions of this Agreement and to confer with the employee during working 
hours.  The representative's activities shall not disrupt the orderly and smooth operation of 
Town government. 
  
ARTICLE III 
HOURS OF WORK 
 
1.  Employee’s minimum basic work week shall be 35 hours per week.  There shall 
be no maximum number of hours of work per week.  Employee shall not receive additional 
compensation for ho liday pay.  Employee is not entitled to earn, accrue, or be paid for 
overtime or compensatory time.  
 
2.  Employee shall be entitled to the same paid holidays as the employees under his 
supervision. 
 
3. (a) Five (5) days personal leave will be granted.  This shall be prorated in “Year” 
(year of hire) beginning the first full month of employment.  
 
    (b)  Personal leave may not be accumulated and must be used within the 
calendar year earned, except that unused personal days at the end of each year shall 
be converted to sick time and may be used as sick time, subject to all the rules and 
pertaining to sick time. 
 
    (c)  Personal leave must be approved by the Town Supervisor  or Designee.  
Employee must request such leave at least forty -eight (48) hours in advance unless the 
personal leave is deemed to be an emergency of which he  had no prior knowled ge, in 
which case Employee must notify the Supervisor or designee of such absence.  Failure to 
notify the Supervisor or designee of his absence will result in loss of pay fo r the day's 
absence. 
 
4.  Funeral Leave.  Employee shall be entitled to four (4) consecutive working days 
leave of absence computed either from the day of de ath or the day following death, at  
Employee’s option, for the death of Employee’s spouse, child (including adopted children), 
father, mother, brother, sister, parents, parents-in-law, grandparents, grandparents-in-law, 
9.15.a
Packet Pg. 110
Attachment: Employment Contract Tim Allen  (2025-294 : Ratifies Setting Terms and Conditions of Employment for Sewer District
 
grandchildren, daughter-in-law, brother-in-law, sister-in-law, son-in-law, or stepchild. Such 
leave may be deferred to days surrounding a subsequent memorial service upon approval 
of the Supervisor or his designee. 
 
5.  Jury Service.  Employee will be paid his regular salary while performing jury 
service upon documentary proof being filed with the Supervisor.  Employee shall endorse 
the jury salary checks to the Town.  Travel allowance or mileage compensation checks for 
jury service are to be retained by Employee. 
 
6.  Court Appearance.   Employee’s absence by reason of appearance as a 
defendant or witness on behalf of the Town in any court action involving the Town will be 
approved by the Town Supervisor for the number of days necessary.  Employee shall not 
lose any salary there from. 
 
7.  Parentage Leave.  Employee shall receive a parentage leave as defined in the 
2011-2014 CSEA contract, Article III, Section 5. 
 
ARTICLE IV 
VACATIONS 
 
1.  Employee shall be entitled to 30 working days' vacation (January 1 to December 
31).  This shall be prorated in  “Year” (year of hire)  beginning the first full month of 
employment.  
 
2.  Employee, upon request, shall be paid his vacation pay prior to the vacation, 
providing he shall have given three (3) weeks' written notice to the Supervisor. 
 
3.  Upon retirement or termination of service, except for cause, Employee shall be 
compensated, in cash, for any accumulated vacation not to exceed 60 days. 
 
4.  Employee may carry over any unused vacation days from one (1) year into the 
following year, but in no event shall Employee carry over more than sixty (60) vacation days 
from one year to the next. 
 
            5.  Employee, at his option, shall be entitled to make an election to work the 
current year's allotted vacation time.  Employee must provide written notification to the 
Supervisor of the exercising of this option not fewer than thirty (30) days prior to the date 
of which payment is requested. The Supervisor is to acknowledge  receipt of this 
notification to the payroll personnel prior to payment. Payment is to be processed during 
the next overtime run. Payment will be the same method as outlined in the 2012-2015 
Superior Officers' Contract, Article IX, Section B, except that the buyback shall be in 
blocks of three days per month. In addition, employee must advise the Town in writing, by 
no later than September 1 prior to the year in which the election is being made, on a form 
to be prepared by the Town, of the total minimum and the maximum do llar amounts of 
eligible vacation time and/or sick leave, as appropriate, that the employee will buyout and 
for which he will be paid in the next fiscal year. If the employee does not comply with this 
requirement, then the employee will not be eligible for any accrued time buyout in the next

Attachment: Employment Contract Tim Allen  (2025-294 : Ratifies Setting Terms and Conditions of Employment for Sewer District
 
fiscal year.  
 
ARTICLE V 
SICK LEAVE 
 
1.  Sick leave is absence necessitated by  Employee’s illness or other physical 
disability.  Sick leave will be accumulated at the rate of one and one quarter (1 1/2) days 
per month or (eighteen [18] days per year) beginning the first full month of employment, 
total accumulated sick leave of three hundred (300) days.  After three hundred (300) days, 
additional paid sick leave may be granted in the sole discretion of the Town Board.  In order 
to receive sick le ave, Employee shall, when absent because of sickness for more than 
three (3) days, furnish the Supervisor, when requested by him, with a medical certificate.  
Failure to furnish a medical certificate will result in loss of pay for absent days.  The Town 
Board, in its discretion, may request a physical examination of Employee before his return 
to work. 
 
2.  Employee, or his legal representative, upon retirement or severance, is entitled to 
cash payment for accumulated sick leave.  Said payment(s) shall be paid at the rate of pay 
at time of retirement and shall be payable in  one lump sum payment upon retirement or not 
more than four payments within two years from retirement or severance,  with the value of 
his accumulated and unused sick leave to the extent of one hundred (100%) percent of the 
first two hundred and eighty days (280) thereof  calculated at the rate of pay at time of 
retirement or seve rance same as outlined in the  202 1-2026 Superior Officer ’s 
Contract, Article XI Sectio n C, and as may be amended . Employee must advise 
Accounting Department, in writing within 120 days after retirement, the amount of the first 
payment and the remainder schedule of payments to be paid within two years of retirement 
unless employee selects a date prior to the end of two-year period; and 
 
3. The parties mutually agree that excessive absenteeism due to abuse of sick 
leave should be discouraged. Therefore, the Town may request a doctor's certificate 
from chronic abusers of sick leave (e.g., numerous illness absences even though the 
employee has accumulated sick leave),  regardless of the length of the illness.  An 
employee submitting a claim based on a false statement, or covering a period during which 
the employee  was not actually disabled, will be considered as abusing the sick leave 
provision. E m p lo ye e s who abuse the sick leave provision shall be subject to 
disciplinary action. 
 
4.  Employee may elect to reduce the sick time accrued under paragraph "1" one 
by filing a written election with the Supervisor one (1) month prior to payment.  Buy-out 
shall be in lots of ten (10) sick days. No buy-out shall be permitted unless at the time 
of election Employee has accumulated at least fifty (50) sick days. The rate of pay and 
payment method will be the same as outlined in the 2021-2026 Superior Officer’s Contract, 
Article XI Section C.

ARTICLE VI 
GRIEVANCE PROCEDURE 
 
1.  Consideration of Grievance. 
 
A grievance by Employee shall be made, in writing, to the Town Board.  Upon 
receipt of the grievance, the Town Board ma y request Employee to submit any ag reed 
statement of facts or his version of the facts, or any other documents that the Town Board 
may deem pertinent to the determination of the appeal. 
The Town Board shall conduct a hearing within twenty (20) business days of receipt 
of an appeal.  Within twenty (20) business days after the hearing, the Town Board shal l 
make a decision based on its findings an d advise Employee.  The decision of the Town 
Board shall be final and all parties bound thereby. 
 
2.  Time of Hearings. 
 
All discu ssions and hearing s shall, so far as practicable, be conducted during 
working hours. 
 
3.  Representation. 
 
    Employee shall have the right at all times to representation of his choosing. 
 
4.  Limitations. 
 
If a grievance occurs and cannot be resolved immediately, Employee shall obey all 
directives and shall present the grievance as soon thereafter as practicable.  Grievances 
which are not presented within ten (10) days of the occurrence shall be deemed to have 
been abandoned. 
 
5.  Withdrawn Grievances. 
 
    Employee may withdraw a grievance at any point in the grievance procedure. 
 
ARTICLE VII 
PENSION AND LONGEVITY 
 
Employee represents that he  is a member of the New York State Employees 
Retirement System.  As a Tier IV employee, he is a participant in the Article 14 or Article 15 
Coordinated Retirement Plan. 
 
Longevity payments shall b e b ased o n the present year’s sa lary and the 
percentages shall be taken there from.  Employee shall be paid longevity based on the 
following schedule: 
 
Four percent (4%) of base pay after ten (10) years of consecutive service.

Seven percent (7%) of base pay after eighteen (18) years of consecutive service. 
 
        It is understo od and agreed by and between the partie s that Allen’s prior

ARTICLE VIII 
HEALTH INSURANCE 
 
1.  The Town shall pay, on Employee’s behalf, one hundred (100%) percent of the 
cost of either the individual or family coverage for hospitalization under the Town Health 
Insurance Program.  The Town shall pay for one hundred (100%) percent coverage for  
Employee if he retires from the Town and the Town shall also pay to the  extent of fifty 
(50%) percent coverage on the premiums for his family. 
 
If Employee and his spouse, if employed through the Town, are currently receiving 
(or are eligible to receive ) family health benefits through the Town, only one will be 
permitted to continue t o receive family level coverage.  In this event, the  person whose 
coverage changes from family to individual or no coverage will be e ntitled to the health 
insurance buy-out, provided that he: (1) has submitted to the Town documentation showing 
that he/she has health insurance coverage; and (b) remains in changed status for a period 
of 12 consecuti ve months.  The 12 -month per iod will  coincide with the annual option 
transfer period.   Payment will be made annually during the June or Decem ber first 
following the end of the 12-month period, provided that Employee or his spouse remains in 
the changed status. The employee may reinstate coverage within the 12-month period if he 
experiences a qualifying event and has submitted to the Town adequate documentation of 
that event, consistent with the rules and regulations of the Town’s health insurance plan 
and applicable laws and regulations.   
 
At retirement, the former employee who is otherwise eligible for family retiree health 
insurance coverage through the Town but for the operation of this provision shall continue 
to be ineligible for family retiree health insurance coverage through the Town.  However, 
during retirement, the former employee may reinstate his  own family health insuran ce 
coverage, if the former employee has dependents as defined in the Plan, in the event of an 
emergency causing the loss of the other person’s Town health insurance, consistent with 
the rules and regulations of the Town’s health insurance plan and applicab le laws and 
regulations. 
 
In the event that Employee’s   employment with the Town should terminate, he shall 
have the option, at his own expense, to participate in the Town Health Insurance Program, 
consistent with applicable laws, rules and regulations.   
 
The service requirement for receipt of health insurance in retirement shall be 
ten  consecutive years of service with the Town. However, if Employee leaves Town 
service, he  must continue with NYSHIP in vested status by paying the entire cost of 
coverage, or by being enrolled as an e m p l o y e e at a subsequent participating

Packet Pg. 114
Attachment: Employment Contract Tim Allen  (2025-294 : Ratifies Setting Terms and Conditions of Employment for Sewer District
 
agency or by being enrolled as a dependent on a NYSHIP policy in order to retain 
eligibility for retiree health benefits through the Town. If Employee leaves to work for 
another NYSHIP employer, he  is not eligible for retiree health insurance if he vests 
with the second employer 
 
2.  The Town shall pay, on Employee’s behalf, one hundred (100%) percent of the 
cost of either the individual or family plan for dental coverage under the Riverhead Town 
Dental Plan.  If Employee and his spouse, if employed through the Town, are  currently 
receiving (or are eligible to receive) family dental insurance benefits through the Town, only 
one will be permitted to continue to receive family level coverage.  In this event, the person 
whose coverage changes from family to individual coverage or no coverage will be entitled 
to the dental insurance buy-out.  Should that person choose to decline to receive individual 
coverage, then that person will be eligible for the buy-out of the individual coverage. 
 
3.  The Town shall pay, on Employee’s behalf, one hundred (100%) percent of the 
cost of either the individual or family plan for optical coverage under the Riverhead Town 
Optical Plan.  If Employee and his spouse, if employed through the Town, are  currently 
receiving (or are eligible to receive) family optical insurance benefits through the Town, only 
one will be permitted to continue to receive family level coverage.  In this event, the person 
whose coverage changes from family to individual coverage or no coverage will be entitled 
to the optical insurance buy-out.  Should that person choose to decline to receive individual 
coverage, then that person will be eligible for the buy-out of the individual coverage. 
 
4.  The Town will insure Employee’s life in accordance with the maximum death 
benefit provided by the Employees Retirement System for Tier IV members.   
 
5.  Employee, at his option, may elect not to accept the Town's hospitalizati on 
coverage for a period of not less than one calendar year and receive the following payment 
during the first full pay period of each year the electi on is made: $1,650 .00 if Employee 
changes from family to no coverage; $900.00 if Employee changes from family to individual 
coverage; $750.00 if Employee changes from individual to no coverage. Also, at his option, 
Employee may elect not to accept the dental coverage for a period o f not less than one 
calendar year and receive the following payment during the first full pay period of each year 
the election is made:  $230.00 if Employee changes from family to no coverage; $150.00 if 
Employee changes from family to individual coverage; $80.00 if Employee changes from 
individual to no coverage. Also, at his option, Employee may elect not to accept the optical 
coverage for a period of not less than one calendar year and receive a payment of twenty-
five dollars ($25.00) during the first f ull pay period of each year the election is made. 
Employee must sign an application form each year and said application shall include an 
acknowledgment that he is covered under another plan. 
 
6.  The Town will offer a Universal Life Insurance Policy, a disability insurance policy 
or participation in the New York State def erred compensation program.  The employee 
may, at his option , choose the life insurance, the dis ability i nsurance, the deferr ed 
compensation pro gram, any com bination thereof,  or, ha ve the Town  contribute to an 
independent life insurance policy, disability insurance policy , an nuity or deferred 
compensation program of the employee ’s choice and adjusted annually.  A ny additional

ARTICLE IX 
GENERAL PROVISIONS 
 
1.  The Town agrees to provide legal counsel to defend  Employee in any action 
arising out of an as sault on Employee while on Town bu siness, and the Town hereby 
agrees to defend, indemnify, and hold Employee harmless for any and all acts performed 
for the Town, its agents and employees, including but  not limited to preparation, 
certification and sealing of pl ans prepared exclusively for  the Town, its agents and 
employees, provided Employee was acting within the scope of his employment.  In the 
event tha t Employee is appointed, authorized or dir ected by the Town or one of its 
agencies to represent it as a m ember of the board of direct ors of an organization or 
agency, then he shall be covered by the provisions of Public Officers Law Section 18 and 
Town Code Sections 15 -1 and 15 -2 pertaining to th e defense and indemnification of 
officers and employees of p ublic entities, provided  Employee is otherwise eligible for 
coverage pursuant to the terms of those provisions. 
 
2.  If Employee is injured or assaulted in the course of employment, he shall receive 
100% of his salary for the first six months during which he is absent from work, and 85% of 
his salary for any time beyond tha t per iod, until such time as his application for 
reinstatement to full duty status, or, in the event of permanent disability, his application for a 
disability pension be finally determined or  by a physician's examination determining no 
further disability, whichever comes first.  If Employee is injured on the job and reports the 
same to the Supervisor, and has to be absent from work, no days shall be deducted from 
his sick leave for such injury.  If Employee receives a compensation check for lost time due 
to a compensable injury, he shall endorse his check over to the Town.  The above shall 
apply if Employee was acting within the scope of his employment.  Nothing contained 
herein shall in any way be deemed to restrict the Town’ s right to separat e Employee 
pursuant to the provisions of Civil Service Law Sections 71-73. 
 
3.  A leave of absence, without pay, may be granted to Employee in the discretion of 
the Town Board for a maximum of six (6) months, upon written application therefore and 
good cause shown. 
 
4.  If Employee is absent without leave or without due notification to the Supervisor, 
he shall suffer loss of pay for the days of such absence.  
 
5.  Employee will be paid every two (2) weeks on Thursday of the latter week.   
 
6.  Upon Employee’s request to examine his official employment personnel file, he 
may be permitted to do so at the discretion of the Town Board.  Any material classified as 
confidential sh all not be subject to duplication by  Employee, but he  shall have an 
opportunity to read said material and make a written reply, which shall be inserted in his 
9.15.a
Packet Pg. 116
Attachment: Employment Contract Tim Allen  (2025-294 : Ratifies Setting Terms and Conditions of Employment for Sewer District
 
personnel folder. 
 
7.  To the extent permitted by the U.S. In ternal Revenue Code and the New York 
State Income Tax Laws, the Town shall permit Employee to establish  a deferred 
compensation plan for said employee. 
 
8.  The Town will provide reimbursement for all professional continuing education, 
license and association fees related to and in furtherance of the Sewer Wastewater Plant 
Operator 4/A position not to exceed $1,200.00 annually.  Payment will only be made upon 
submission of voucher. 
 
 
ARTICLE X 
WAGES 
 
  Allen shall receive the following annual salary (January 1 through December 31 
each year: $162,000.00. This salary shall be pro-rated in the year 2025 with an effective 
date commencing March 22, 2025.  
 
Effective January 1, 2026, Allen’s salary will be increased annually based on the 
consumer price index for New York, Northern New Jersey, and Long Island limited and not 
to exceed 3.5% or equal to the CSEA salary and Step increases, whichever is greater. 
 
   Allen’s base salary for each remaining year of this Agreement shall not be less 
than that of the preceding year.

Councilwoman Waski offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilman Rothwell

Riverhead established the Emerging Technology Committee; and

serving on the Emerging Technology Committee; and 
 
WHEREAS, the Town Board wishes to appoint Tracy Stark-James to the 
Emerging Technology Committee as Chairperson, for a five-year term that will expire 
July 1, 2029.

appoints Tracy Stark-James to the Town of Riverhead Emerging Technology 
Committee and appoints the following individuals to such committee without 
compensation, subject to the following term periods, and serving at the pleasure of the 
Town Board; and

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and 
obtain a copy of this resolution from the electronic storage device, and if needed, a 
certified copy of same may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk.

TB Resolution 2025-300 
 
APPROVES SPECIAL EVENT CHAPTER 255 APPLICATION FOR HALLOCKVILLE 
MUSEUM FARM (FLEECE AND FIBER FESTIVAL) 
 
Councilman Rothwell offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilman Kern 
 
WHEREAS, on March 12, 2025, Heather Johnson on behalf of Hallockville 
Museum Farm, submitted a Chapter 255 Application for the purpose of conducting A 
Fleece and Fiber Festival at 6038 Sound Avenue, Jamesport, New York, on May 17, 
2025, between the hours of 10:00 am to 4:00 pm with a rain date on May 18, 2024 and 
 
WHEREAS, the applicant has paid the requisite Chapter 255 Application fee of 
$175.00; and 
 
WHEREAS, a certificate of insurance naming the Town of Riverhead as an 
additional insured has been received; and   
 
NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Town Board of the Town of 
Riverhead hereby has classified the action as a Type II under SEQRA NYCRR 617.5 C 
(21) and requiring no further environmental review; and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that the C hapter 255 Application of Hallockville Museum Farm for 
the purpose of conducting a Fleece and Fiber Festival at 6038 Sound Avenue, 
Jamesport, New York, on the aforesaid date and time, is hereby approved; and be it 
further 
 
RESOLVED, that any tent installations, including the obtainment of any 
necessary tent permits, and any all electric shall comply with the applicable provisions 
of the Building and Fire Code of New York State, the National Electrical Code and 
National Fire Protection Association 102 (Tents & Membrane Structures); and be it 
further 
 
RESOLVED, that this approval is subject to the provisions of Riverhead Town 
Code Chapter 301-251 G (7) entitled “Signs” and any other section of the Riverhead 
Town Code that may pertain to this event; and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that the Outdoor Safety Plan submitted with the applicant’s Chapter 
255 Application is subject to the review and approval of the Riverhead Fire Marshal; and 
be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that should it be determined that police and or fire mar shal 
personnel and vehicle usage become necessary for this event, then in that instance, 
Hallockville Museum Farm agrees to pay the costs associated with same, which shall 
9.21
Packet Pg. 129
become due and payable upon delivery of an invoice to them for those additional cost s; 
and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that all events taking place on Town property may be contingent 
upon the execution of a License Agreement with the Town of Riverhead within 7 days of 
the event and a fee of not less than $100.00; and be it further, 
 
RESOLVED, that all events taking place on Town property that will have the sale 
or consumption of alcohol are contingent on NYS Liquor Authority approval for on -site 
consumption; and be it further, 
 
RESOLVED, that the Town Supervisor is authorized to execute a lic ense 
agreement for the use of Town property as well as with participating alcohol service 
vendors in a form to be approved by the Town Attorney’s Office; and be it further,  
 
RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is hereby authorized to forward a copy of this 
resolution to Chief of Police, Edward Frost, Chief Fire Marshal, Andrew Smith and  
Hallockville Museum Farm, Attn: Heather Johnson execdirector@hallockville.org , and 
be it further  
 
RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of 
this resolution from the electronic storage device and, if needed, a copy of same may be 
obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk.   
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Kenneth Rothwell, Councilman 
SECONDER: Robert Kern, Councilman 
AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

elections for the 2025 calendar year with an option to renew for the 2026 calendar year; 
and

Riverhead Town Hall as an early polling place to allow for the Primary Election Early Voting  and for 
General Election Early Voting on the dates of June 14, 2025, June 15, 2025, June 16, 2025, June 17, 
2025, June 18, 2025, June 19, 2025, June 20, 2025, June 21, 2025, June 22, 2025, October 25,

Polling Place Agreement; and 
 
WHEREAS, the Town of Riverhead desires to provide such use of the basement-level 
cafeteria at the Riverhead Town Hall, 4 West Second Street, Riverhead, New York 11901 to SCBOE 
as provided in accordance with the terms and conditions set forth in the Early Voting Polling Place 
Agreement. 
 
NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Town Board, be and hereby, authorizes 
the Supervisor to execute the Early Voting Polling Place Agreement for use of the Riverhead Town 
Hall  in substantially the same form annexed hereto for the Primary Election Early Voting  and for 
General Election Early Voting on the dates of June 14, 2025, June 15, 2025, June 16, 2025, June 17, 
2025, June 18, 2025, June 19, 2025, June 20, 2025, June 21, 2025, June 22, 2025, October 25, 
2025, October 26, 2025, October 27, 2025, October 28, 2025, October 29, 2025, October 30, 2025, 
October 31, 2025, November 1, 2025 and November 2, 2025 at hours set forth in the Early Voting 
Polling Place Agreement and including an option to renew for the 2026 calendar year; and 
be it further, 
 
RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is hereby directed to forward a copy of this 
resolution to the Office of the Town Attorney; and be it further, 
 
RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of this resolution

LICENSE AGREEMENT 
This LICENSE AGREEMENT (hereinafter “License”) made this 15th day of  May , 2024, 
by and between the Town of Riverhead, a municipal corporation of the State of New York, 
with offices located at 4 West Second Street, Riverhead, New York 11901 (hereinafter 
"Licensor”) and Riverhead Industrial Development Agency, a public benefit agency 
created and established in 1980 by an act of the State of New York with its principal office 
located at 542 East Main Street, Suite 1, Riverhead, NY 11901 (hereinafter “Licensee”).  
WHEREAS, the Town of Riverhead is the owner of a building located at 55 Columbus 
Avenue, Riverhead, New York and the Town of Riverhead maintains said building; and   
WHEREAS, the Riverhead Industrial Development Agency expressed a desire to enter 
into a license agreement for space that is presently vacant and not needed for municipal 
purpose at 55 Columbus Avenue, Riverhead, New York as described and depicted in 
Exhibit A; and 
WHEREAS, the Town Board consulted with the Riverhead Industrial Development  
Agency and the Town Engineering Department and determined that a license agreement 
with Riverhead Industrial Development Agency is in the best interests of the Town; and 
NOW THEREFORE, in consideration of the mutual promises made herein, it is agreed as 
follows: 
ARTICLE I 
General Description of License Agreement 
1. Description of Licensed Premises: Town of Riverhead owns and maintains the building, 
including parking area, walkways, lawn area, commonly known and referred to as Town 
Hall West located at 55 C olumbus Avenue, Riverhead, NY (hereinafter referred to as 
"Licensed Premises").   
2.  Use of Licensed Premises:  Town of Riverhead (hereinafter referred to as "Licensor" 
or "Town") licenses to the Riverhead Industrial Development Agency (hereinafter 
"Licensee") a revocable, non-assignable and non-exclusive use of the Licensed Premises 
(including the parking area, walkways, lawn area). Licensee shall be prohibited from using 
the premises as a residence, place of lodging, bed & breakfast etc. nor may Licensee  
operate any other business or commercial activity on the subject property. Licensee shall 
not be permitted to and shall not allow others to use the premises for any other purpose.  
It is understood and agreed, the Licensor has made no representation regar ding: 
improvements or condition of building or parking area nor has licensee relied upon any 
such representation by the Town and instead Licensee bears sole responsibility for 
investigation as to such issues related to the intended use and operation of the  above 
described areas related to activities of Licensee. Licensor will maintain sole use and 
occupancy of the basement.  Licensee shall be responsible to determine, set and/or 
adjust Licensee employee’s use of the parking area to ensure that safe access t o and 
from the premises by Licensee and its employees.   
9.25.a
Packet Pg. 147
Attachment: IDA and TOR Agreement for Rec bldg DRAFT  (2025-304 : Ratifies Authorization for the Supervisor to Execute a License Agreement
 
 
3.  Term of the License: The initial term of this License (the “term”) shall be for   Five (5  ) 
years commencing on or about May 15, 2024 and shall end on or about May 14, 2029.  
This Agreement shal l be automatically extended for one year unless on or before the 
expiration of any extended term either Party provides to the other written notice of its 
desire not to automatically renew this Agreement. Further, Licensee agrees that in the 
event that the Licensor shall determine that the licensed space is required for other 
legitimate municipal purpose, the Licensor may terminate this license agreement with 180 
days written notice. Upon expiration of the original term of the license or termination of 
the license agreement, Licensee shall remove all equipment, improvements, stock etc. 
(*Licensee must return licensed premises to broom clean, vacant condition) from licensed 
premises within fifteen days after expiration of the term of the license, Licensee shal l be 
required to pay a fee of $100.00 (One Hundred Dollars) per day or such portion thereof 
for each day the equipment/improvements/stock continues to remain at the licensed 
premises beyond the 15 day grace period set forth in the preceding sentence. In the event 
Licensee fails to remove the equipment/improvements/stock within a month of the 
expiration or termination of the term of the license, the Town shall be entitled to remove 
the equipment/improvements/stock and access all charges set forth above, together with 
expenses/charges/costs related to the removal, relocation and storage of the 
equipment/improvements/stock to the Licensee and the expenses so assessed shall 
constitute a lien against the Licensee. 
4. License Fee:  Licensee agrees to pay Licensor the sum of $400.00 per month, with the 
first payment due upon execution of this agreement and the remaining payments in 
advance on the fifteenth day of each month during the term of the license. 
Notwithstanding the above, to the extent Licensee, with conse nt of Licensor, takes 
possession prior to execution of this Agreement, Licensee shall be responsible for 
payment of the monthly fee from date of possession of the premises. The payments shall 
be mailed to Town of Riverhead, 4 West Second Street, Riverhead, NY 11901 Attention:  
Office of the Town Attorney.    
5.  Security Deposit:  None.    
ARTICLE II 
Terms, Conditions, Restrictions for Use of Licensed Premises 
1.  Use and Occupancy:  
A. Licensee agrees to use and occupy the premises pursuant to all rules and regulations 
prescribed by the Town, all statutes, ordinances, rules, regulations and directions in 
existence during the periods covered by the License, made or issued by the federal, state 
or local governmental agencies or departments.  
B. Licensee shall not assign, transfer, mortgage, or otherwise dispose of or encumber 
this License or any rights without the prior written consent of the Town. Any such attempt 
without consent of the  Town shall be an automatic revocation of this License and all 
payments received by the Town shall be forfeited to the Town as liquidated damages.  
9.25.a
Packet Pg. 148
Attachment: IDA and TOR Agreement for Rec bldg DRAFT  (2025-304 : Ratifies Authorization for the Supervisor to Execute a License Agreement
 
 
C.  Licensee agrees that in the event that Licensor requires use of a portion of the building 
to host a clas s, meeting or such other event, Licensee shall make every effort to 
accommodate such municipal use of the subject premises. Licensor shall notify Licensee 
30 days prior to any such scheduled class or meeting and provide detail regarding time, 
number of participants, etc.  
D. The Licensee and the Town agree that nothing contained in this agreement is intended, 
or shall be construed as, creating or establishing a partnership or joint venture between 
the parties here or as designating the Licensee as the agent or representative of the Town 
for any purpose beyond what is previously recognized by the Town of Riverhead in 
Resolution #113 of 1980 establishing the Town of Riverhead Industrial Development 
Agency.  
2.  Alterations: Licensee shall not remove, alter or modify any existing improvement on 
the subject premises (building, parking area, walkways, and lawn areas) nor permanently 
attach, affix, or permit to be permanently attached or affixed upon the premises, or if it is 
necessary to permanently attach, affix, relocate, replace, alter or modify the premises for 
operation of Licensee or related to the safety of pedestrian and/or motor vehicle traffic, 
Licensee shall obtain consent, in writing,  from the Town after review and comment by 
the Engineering Department . In connection with such improvements, alterations or 
installation of fixtures, the Town may require submission of proposed designs, 
construction plans, specifications and contract documents for approval and incorporate 
all or part of them within this agr eement as attachments.  Licensee shall remove all 
equipment and structures from the licensed premises upon the expiration or termination 
of the license agreement. In the event Licensee fails to remove the equipment and 
structures from licensed premises wit hin five days after expiration of the term of the 
license, Licensee shall be required to pay a fee of $100.00 (One Hundred Dollars) per 
day or such portion thereof for each day the equipment/structures continues to remain at 
the licensed premises. In the e vent Licensee fails to remove the equipment/structures 
within a month of the expiration or cancellation of the term of the license, the Town shall 
be entitled to remove the equipment/structures and access all charges set forth above, 
together with expenses /charges/costs related to the removal, relocation and storage of 
the equipment/structures to the Licensee and the expenses so assessed shall constitute 
a lien against the Licensee.    
3. Maintenance: The Licensee has inspected the licensed premises, including the parking 
area and accepts same “as is”(the park and recs stuff needs to be removed) .  The 
Licensee, at its own expense, shall keep the premises in good repair and agrees to 
surrender the premises to the Town at the end of each and every term of thi s license in 
the same condition as at the beginning of the term, ordinary wear and use being excepted, 
and shall pay for all damages occasioned by its use.  
4.  Utility Services: All utility services including electric, water, and *sewer (if applicable), 
for or in connection with the operation and maintenance of the licensed premises are 
included in the license fee as set forth above, except Licensee shall be responsible for its 
own cable television and internet service. Town will in no event be liable for any 
9.25.a
Packet Pg. 149
Attachment: IDA and TOR Agreement for Rec bldg DRAFT  (2025-304 : Ratifies Authorization for the Supervisor to Execute a License Agreement
 
 
interruption or failure of utility services or internet services on the premises or pay for any 
installation of any utility or internet services.  
5.  Indemnification and Insurance:    
 A.  Licensee shall use the premises so as not to endanger any pers on and 
Licensee agrees to protect, indemnify, hold harmless and defend the Town from any and 
all liability, damage or expense by reason of any injury or injuries sustained by anyone to 
persons or property or loss of property received, done or occurring in or about the 
premises licensed by the Licensee, including designation of entrance and exits, or any 
liability sustained during the operation of Licensee's business, excluding that caused by 
or resulting from the negligence of the Town and its agents, servants or employees.  
 B.  Insurance: The Licensee shall secure, maintain and furnish, at its sole cost and 
expense, during and throughout the License term general liability policies insuring 
Licensee and naming Licensor as additional insured. The liability p olicy shall be one 
which shall afford bodily injury coverage in an amount of not less than $1,000,000.00 per 
occurrence and $2,000,000.00 aggregate for more than one person involved in any one 
accident and not less than $500,000.00 for damage to property. The insurance coverage 
shall be primary insurance and/or primary source of recovery as respects to the Town of 
Riverhead with respect to all claims, losses or liability arising directly or indirectly from 
Licensee’s use of the premises and parking area loc ated at 55 Columbus Avenue, 
Riverhead, NY.  Any insurance or self-insurance maintained by the Town shall be excess 
of the licensee’s insurance and shall not contribute with it. Licensee shall secure and 
deliver to the Town of Riverhead a general liability special endorsement reflecting the 
above, together with a certificate of liability insurance mirroring said endorsement prior to 
any activity, improvement or use of the licensed space.   
In addition to the above, Licensee shall secure, maintain and furnish  the following 
additional insurances:   
1) Worker's Compensation   
Worker's Compensation Insurance, in statutory amounts, covering all employees who are 
to provide a service under this agreement. Employer's Liability Coverage with limits of not 
less than $250,000 for each accident or illness shall be included.  
2) Commercial Liability (Primary and Umbrella).  
Commercial Liability Insurance or equivalent with limits of not less than $1,000,000 per 
occurrence, combined single limit, for bodily injury, personal injury, and property damage 
liability. Products/completed operation, independent contractor, and contractual liability 
coverage are to be included.  
3) Property Insurance  
Such insurance shall include but not be limited to liability or property damage, loss of life, 
bodily injury or illness, property damage to all structures on the subject property, 
sidewalks, and other fixed or movable property which shall include the Town of Riverhead 
as additional named insured.  
9.25.a
Packet Pg. 150
Attachment: IDA and TOR Agreement for Rec bldg DRAFT  (2025-304 : Ratifies Authorization for the Supervisor to Execute a License Agreement
 
 
  C. The Licensee will furnish the Town , the original Certificates of Insurance 
evidencing the required coverage to be in force on the date of this agreement, and 
Renewal Certificates of Insurance, or such similar evidence, if the coverage has an 
expiration or renewal date occurring during the term of this agreement.  
      D.  The insurance shall provide for sixty days prior written notice to be given to the 
Town in the event coverage is substantially changed, cancelled, or nonrenewal.  
       E.  The Licensee agrees that insurer shall waive it s rights of subrogation against 
the Town.  
 F. The Licensee expressly understands and agrees that any insurance maintained 
by the Town shall apply in excess of and not contribute with insurance provided by the 
Licensee under the agreement.  
 G. The Town ma intains the right to modify, delete, alter or change these 
requirements.  
 H.   Licensee shall not occupy the premises licensed under this lease until all 
required insurance is in full force and effect and submitted to the Town.  
 I.  The Licensee's obliga tion to the Town for any liability, damage or expense by 
reason of any injury or injuries sustained by anyone to persons or property or loss or 
property received, done or occurred on or about the premises licensed by the Licensee 
shall not be limited by or to the coverage provided in the General Liability Insurance policy 
required to be furnished by the Licensee to the Town.  
9. Assignment; Sublicense: The Licensee may not assign, transfer, or otherwise dispose 
of or encumber the licensed premises nor name or utilize the licensed premises as part 
of any application, permit, license, land use related to operation of Licensee’s businesses 
or operations.   
10. Licensor’s Right of Access: The Licensor, or the Licensor’s employees or agents, shall 
have the right to enter the licensed space at any time for emergencies or with seventy 
two (72) hour notice to Licensee. Notwithstanding the above, the Licensor shall use 
reasonable efforts to minimize any disruption of the Licensee’s activities.  
11.  Default Provisions:  
 A.  Any waiver or any breach of covenants contained herein to be kept and 
performed by Licensee, shall not be deemed or considered as a continuing waiver and 
shall not operate to bar or prevent the Town from proceeding under the provisions of this 
agreement.  
       B. As set forth above, upon termination of the License, whether caused by lapse 
of time or otherwise, Licensee shall at once surrender possession of the premises. If  
possession is not immediately surrendered, the Town may take possession of the 
premises and expel or remove Licensee and those claiming by, through, or under it, by 
force if necessary, without civil or criminal liability.  
9.25.a
Packet Pg. 151
Attachment: IDA and TOR Agreement for Rec bldg DRAFT  (2025-304 : Ratifies Authorization for the Supervisor to Execute a License Agreement
 
 
      C. Upon the breach of any covenant or condition contained herein, the Town shall 
give written notice to Licensee of the breach. Licensee agrees that it will remedy the 
breach within thirty days. If the breach of any covenant or condition is not cured within the 
above time, the Town  reserves the right to revoke this agreement and Licensee agrees 
to surrender the premises. Any license fees previously received by the Town shall be 
retained by the Town as liquidated damages.  
 D. Licensee shall pay and discharge all costs, expenses, and attorney's fees which 
might be incurred by the Town in enforcing the covenants of this License Agreement.  
 E. The remedies here created are cumulative and the use of one remedy shall not 
be taken to exclude or waive the right to the use of another remedy.  
 F.  In the event that the License is granted to more than one individual or other 
legal entity (or to any combination), then and in that event, each and every obligation or 
undertaking to be performed by Licensee under the License Agreement shall be the joint 
and several obligation of each such individual or other legal entity.  
12. Miscellaneous:  Notices to the Town provided for herein may be sent by first class 
mail, postage prepaid, addressed to the Office of the Town Attorney, 4 West Second 
Street, Riverhead, NY 11901, Attention:  Office of the Town Attorney. Notice to Licensee 
provided for here may be sent by first class mail, postage prepaid, addressed to Licensee 
at  4 West Second Street, Riverhead, NY 11901. 
IN WITNESS WHEREOF, Licensor a nd Licensee do hereby execute this License 
Agreement as of the date and year first above written. 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD

04.01.2025 ADOPTED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-305 
 
AUTHORIZES SUPERVISOR TO SIGN AUTHORIZATION AGREEMENT WITH LONG 
ISLAND POWER AUTHORITY (LIPA)  FOR 2024-2025 PILOTS 
 
Councilman Kern offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilwoman Merrifield 
 
WHEREAS, there exists an ongoing dispute between the Town of Riverhead, County 
of Suffolk and Long Island Power Authority (LIPA) regarding the manner and method of 
computing, collecting and distributing of monies owed by LIPA pursuant to Public Authorities 
Law and/or in connection with LIPA’s interest in real property located within the Town of 
Riverhead; and 
 
WHEREAS, the parties are desirous of resolving this dispute on an interim basis 
to provide for certain billing, payment, colle ction and distribution of funds for the 
2024/2025 tax year without prejudice to certain ongoing litigation involving the parties. 
 
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED , that based upon the recommendation 
of counsel, the Town Board hereby authorizes the Superviso r to execute an 
Authorization Agreement for the tax year 202 4/2025 with LIPA, the County of Suffolk 
and the relevant taxing districts, in substantially the form annexed hereto; and be it 
further, 
 
 RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is hereby directed to forwar d a copy of this 
resolution to the Town Attorney’s Office; and be it further, 
 
RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of 
this resolution from the electronic storage device and, if needed, a copy of same may be 
obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk. 
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Robert Kern, Councilman 
SECONDER: Denise Merrifield, Councilwoman 
AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

TB Resolution 2025-306 
 
AUTHORIZES EXTENSION OF AGREEMENT WITH  URBAN DESIGN 
ASSOCIATES, LTD 
 
Councilwoman Merrifield offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilwoman Waski 
 
WHEREAS, by Resolutio n #2024-203 adopted on February 21, 2024, the Town 
Board of the Town of Riverhead, authorized the Supervisor to execute a License 
Agreement between the Town and Urban Design Associates, LTD. to provide design 
coordination consulting services relating to va rious projects in the Downtown Riverhead 
area; and 
WHEREAS, the agreement dated February 23, 2024 was for one year and the 
scope of services under this agreement is ongoing and there still remains a significant 
contract balance; and  
 
WHEREAS, Urban Design  Associates, LTD. has continued to provide services 
set forth in the original agreement dated January 23, 2024 and has agreed to extend the 
contract for one (1) year beginning February 23, 2025, subject to the same terms and 
conditions set forth in the original contract. 
 
NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED , that the agreement with Urban Design 
Associates, LTD. be extended for one (1) year beginning February 23, 2025 under the 
same terms and conditions set forth in the original contract; and be it further, 
 
 RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is hereby directed to forward a copy of this 
resolution to Community Development Agency, the Accounting Department; and the 
Office of the Town Attorney; and be it further,    
  
RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review an d obtain a copy of 
this resolution from the electronic storage device, and if needed, a certified copy of the 
same may be obtained from the office of the Town Clerk. 
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Denise Merrifield, Councilwoman 
SECONDER: Joann Waski, Councilwoman 
AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

TB Resolution 2025-307 
 
AUTHORIZES THE SUPERVISOR TO EXECUTE AN ADDENDUM TO AN 
AGREEMENT WITH LVF LANDSCAPE ARCHITECTS, PLLC 
 
Councilwoman Waski offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilman Rothwell 
 
 WHEREAS, The Town of Riverhead executed a Consultant/ Professional 
Services Agreement with LVF Landscape Architects, PLLC dated January 22, 2024 for 
the Planning, Design and Engineering of the Proposed Town Square Adaptive 
Playground adjacent to the planned new Town Square; and 
 
 WHEREAS, LVF Landscape Architects, PLLC has advised the Town of the need 
for additional services necessary to realize the Adaptive Riverfront Playground and 
requests authorization to perform these services which will requir e additional 
compensation in the total amount of $70,157.00; and 
 
 WHEREAS, LVF Landscape Architects, PLLC wishes to add PW Grosser 
Consulting, Inc. as an additional member of its support team tasked with providing the 
additional services including testing  excavated fill, providing a report based on the 
testing results, and preparing demolition/removal and stockpile/erosion control plans; 
and 
 
WHEREAS, PW Grosser Consulting, Inc., has a business address of 630 
Johnson Avenue, Suite 7, Bohemia, New York 11716. 
 
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED,  that LVF Landscape Architects, PLLC 
shall be entitled to additional compensation totaling $70,157.00 for additional services 
necessary to complete the Adaptive Riverfront Playground; and be it further,     
 
RESOLVED, that LVF Landscape Architects, shall add PW Grosser Consulting 
Inc as an additional member of its support team and all terms and conditions of the 
original Consultant/Professional Services Agreement dated January 22, 2024 shall 
remain in full force and effect; and be it further, 
 
RESOLVED, that the Supervisor is hereby authorized to execute an addendum 
to the agreement with LVF Landscape Architects, PLLC in substantially the same form 
as annexed hereto; and be it further,  
 
RESOLVED, that the Town of Riverhead  Financial Administrator hereby has the 
authority to establish the appropriate budget for the revenue and expenditure; and be it 
further, 
 
RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is hereby directed to forward a copy of this 
resolution to Dawn Thomas, CDA Director, Accounting Department and the Office of the

RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of

WHEREAS, on or about January 26, 2021, the Town of Riverhead commenced 
an Article 78 proceeding against the New York State Department of Environmental 
Conservation (NYSDEC) and CMA Mine under Index Nos. 601509/2021; and  
WHEREAS, on or about October 5, 2023, CMA Mine commenced an Article 78 
against the NYSDEC, the Town of Riverhead and Erik Howard, Esq., under Index No.: 
624787/2023; and 
 
WHEREAS, the parties in both actions are desirous of avoiding further time, 
expense, vagaries and uncertainties associated with further litigation and/or trial and 
having entered into negotiations in good faith, acceptable terms of settlement have 
been reached.  
 
 NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED , that based upon the recommendation 
of the T own Attorney in consultation with Special Counsel, David Arntsen, Esq., the 
Town Board authorizes special counsel, David Arntsen, Esq.  to execute the Stipulation 
of Settlement with CMA Mine and Tolling Agreement with CMA Mine and NYSDEC, 
respectively, as a ttached hereto  in connection with the action commenced with the 
actions bearing Suffolk County Index Nos. 601509/2021 and 624787/2023, respectively; 
and be it further,  
 
 RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is hereby directed to forward a copy of this 
resolution to the Town Attorney’s Office, and be it further, 
 
RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of 
this resolution from the electronic storage device and, if needed, a copy of same may be 
obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk.

STIPULATION OF SETTLEMENT OF SPECIAL PROCEEDINGS 
The undersigned counsel for Petitioner Town of Riverhead (“TOWN”) and the undersigned 
counsel for Respondent CMA Mine LLC (“CMA”)  in the Proceeding bearing Index Number 
601509/2021 (“Proceeding 1”), and for Petitioner CMA Mine, LLC (“C MA”) and Respondent s  
Town of Riverhead (“TOWN”), and Erik C. Howard (“HOWARD”)  (together, the “Parties”) in 
the Proceeding Bearing Index Number 624787/2023 (“Proceeding 2) , hereby agree and set forth 
as follows: 
WHEREAS, on or about February 15, 2019, CMA submitted for review by  New York 
State Department of Environmental Conservation (“DEC”)  a mining permit application (NYS 
9.29.a
Packet Pg. 174
Attachment: 250228 Stipulation of Settlement Town CMA Final (1)  (2025-308 : Authorizes Special Counsel to Resolve Pending Litigation)
2 
DEC ID No. 1-4730-00051) to modify an existing mining permit held by CMA (the “Application”) 
for a mine on its property in the TOWN; and 
WHEREAS, on or about September 29, 2020, DEC issued a negative declaration pursuant 
to the State Environmental Quality Review Act  (“SEQRA”) in connection with its review of the 
Application (the “Negative Declaration”); and 
WHEREAS, on or around January 26, 2021, by the filing of its Verified Petition  and 
accompanying documents, the TOWN commenced Proceeding 1 pursuant to Article 78 of the Civil 
Practice Rules and Procedure (“CPLR”) against DEC and CMA, seeking an order from this Court 
annulling the Negative Declaration, which Petition was Amended on February 23, 2024 
(“Proceeding 1”); and 
WHEREAS, during the pendency of Proceeding 1, DEC ceased processing the Application 
pursuant to New York State Environmental Law  §23-2703(3) based on its interpretation of  the 
Decision and Order of the New York State Court of Appeals in Town of Southampton, et al, v New 
York State Department of Environmental Conservation, et al , 39 N.Y.3d 201 (2023)  (“Sand 
Land”); and  
WHEREAS, on April 10, 2023, DEC wrote to the TOWN in accordance with New York 
State Environmental Protection Law §23-2703(3) and its interpretation of Sand Land to inquire as 
to whether the area proposed to be mined in the Application was within the scope of the 
nonconforming use benefitting the property and, as such, permitted under TOWN zoning; and 
WHEREAS, on May 10, 2023, following DEC’s cessation of processing of the 
Application, counsel for CMA wrote to DEC and requested that DEC resume such processing; and 
WHEREAS, on June 5, 2023, the TOWN responded to DEC and advised, amongst other 
things, that CMA had a nonconforming use to  mine within the then permitted  life of mine area, 
9.29.a
Packet Pg. 175
Attachment: 250228 Stipulation of Settlement Town CMA Final (1)  (2025-308 : Authorizes Special Counsel to Resolve Pending Litigation)
3 
but had not established, on the current available records, that CMA had manifested the intention 
to expand its mine beyond its current parameters at such time as the use became nonconforming 
and, therefore, it could not attest on the available records that mi ning was permitted in the area 
proposed to be mined; and 
WHEREAS, on July 3, 2023, DEC wrote to CMA and advised, amongst other things, that 
DEC was prohibited by ECL §23-2703(3) from processing the Application unless and until the 
TOWN determines that the scope of CMA’s nonconforming use extends to the proposed expansion 
contained in the Application; and  
WHEREAS, on or around October 5, 2023, by the filing of its Verified Petition and 
accompanying Documents, CMA commenced Proceeding 2 pursuant to Article 7 8 of the CPLR 
against DEC, the TOWN, and HOWARD, seeking an order from this Court nullifying the 
aforementioned letters from DEC and the TOWN and directing DEC to resume processing the 
Application; and 
WHEREAS, by Order of the Court entered March 27, 2024, Proceeding 1 and Proceeding 
2 were consolidated for joint trial (collectively “Proceedings”); and  
WHEREAS, by Order of the Court dated June 13, 2024,  the Parties were directed, in the 
absence of a settlement of the Proceedings  prior thereto, to appear fo r a settlement conference , 
which settlement conference was held on October 13, 2024, and at which conference counsel and 
their clients/client representatives appeared, and counsel for the parties conferred with each other 
and with the Court; and  
WHEREAS, as a result of conversations between Counsel and the Court , the TOWN and 
CMA agree to discontinue, without prejudice, the Proceedings on specified terms and conditions  
as set forth herein; 
9.29.a
Packet Pg. 176
Attachment: 250228 Stipulation of Settlement Town CMA Final (1)  (2025-308 : Authorizes Special Counsel to Resolve Pending Litigation)
4 
NOW, THEREFORE, in consideration of the foregoing, it is hereby stipulated and agreed, 
by and between the undersigned counsel for the TOWN and CMA, as follows: 
  
1. Upon the execution of this Stipulation of Settlement, the Parties shall discontinue 
Proceeding 1 and Proceeding 2, both without prejudice, and shall file  stipulations of 
discontinuance of the Proceedings with the Court. 
2. CMA shall, within 30 days of the execution of this Stipulation, provide the Town 
Attorney with an application for a letter of preexisting use in a form that shall be provided by the 
TOWN, accompanied by all documents, affidavits and any other supporting evidence 
(“evidence”), including but not limited to all DEC mining permits issued CMA and/or its 
predecessors in interest pertaining to the mine  property, in support of its contention that the 
expansion it seeks, which is the subject of the Application, extends to and is within the scope of 
the nonconforming use that benefits the property. This evidence submitted in connection with the 
application for a letter of preexisting use shall be the record for the purposes of a subsequent appeal 
to the Town Zoning Board of Appeals ("ZBA"), and CMA waives its right to a hearing before the 
ZBA. No fee shall be r equired to be paid by CMA in conjunction with submission of the 
application for a letter with supporting evidence. The Building Inspector and Planning Department 
shall render a determination within 30 days  of the provision of such evidence  to the Town 
Attorney. In the event the application is denied, the denial and application shall be automatically 
converted into an appeal to the Town ZBA.  CMA agrees that it will not utilize any additional 
evidence in any proceeding challenging the ZBA’s determination and decision as to the extent and 
scope of the nonconforming use on the property, which determination and decision shall be made 
in accordance with procedures and timelines to be set forth herein, except for supportive affidavits 
9.29.a
Packet Pg. 177
Attachment: 250228 Stipulation of Settlement Town CMA Final (1)  (2025-308 : Authorizes Special Counsel to Resolve Pending Litigation)
5 
and affirmations which shall make reference to and be limited to the evidence presented to the 
ZBA. If the Building Inspector and Planning Department fail to render a timely determination, the 
application shall be deemed denied unless the parties agree in writing to extend the time for the 
determination(s). 
3. The ZBA shall, within 60 days of determination of the Building Inspector and 
Planning Department  as set forth in paragraph 2 herein, render its written decision and 
determination as to the scope of the nonconforming use that benefits the property, which decision 
and determination shall be transmitted to counsel for CMA and DEC within ten (10) days of its 
issuance. If the ZBA shall fail to render a timely determination, the application shall be deemed 
denied unless the parties agree in writing to extend the time for the determination. 
4. If the ZBA determines that the area on the property into which CMA is seeking to 
expand its mining operation as requested in the Application is within the scope of the 
nonconforming use that benefits the property the TOWN shall, within Ten (10) days of the issuance 
of the ZBA’s decision and determination  state, in a letter to DEC, Division of Environmental 
Permits, Region 1 and DEC’s counsel , that the area proposed to be mined as set forth in the 
application is permissible under Town Zoning Law . Upon receipt of such a letter, DEC may 
resume processing the application in accordance with Article 23 of the New York State 
Environmental Conservation Law and any applicable regulations subject to and without waiver of 
the rights and other provisions set forth in paragraphs 7 and 8 herein.   
5. If the ZBA determines that CMA’s nonconforming use  does not extend to and is 
not within the scope of the area proposed to be mined in the Application, CMA shall have the right 
to challenge such decision and determination in a  proceeding or action in a  Court of competent 
jurisdiction within 30 days of service of the decision upon CMA and/or file an application for an 
9.29.a
Packet Pg. 178
Attachment: 250228 Stipulation of Settlement Town CMA Final (1)  (2025-308 : Authorizes Special Counsel to Resolve Pending Litigation)
6 
expansion of the nonconforming use in accordance with Chapter 301 of the Town Code. Any 
application to expand CMA’s nonconforming use shall be subject to and in compliance with all 
applicable Town Code provisions and fees , and such application shall not be subject to the 
provisions of paragraph 6 herein. The TOWN agrees that it will process CMA’s application for an 
expansion of the nonconforming use in accordance with Chapter 301 of the Town Code whether 
or not a legal challenge by CMA of the TOWN’s decision as to CMA’s nonconforming use on the 
property is commenced. If CMA applies for an expansion of the nonconforming use in accordance 
with Chapter 301 of the Town Code, the TOWN shall, within 60 days of receipt of the expansion 
application, schedule the public hearing required pursuant to 301 of the Town Code and shall there 
after issue its written decision and determination within 45 days, which decision and determination 
shall be transmitted to counsel for CMA within ten (10) days of its issuance . All rights and 
obligations of the parties shall be governed by Chapter 301 and any other applicable provision of 
the Town Code. 
6. The parties expressly agree that the procedures set forth in paragraphs 2-5 of this 
stipulation shall apply in lie u of any procedural provision of the Town Code as pertains to the 
determination of the scope and extent of the nonconforming use benefiting the property. In the 
event that CMA institutes a proceeding or action based upon the ZBA’s determination that CMA’s 
nonconforming use does not extend to and is not within the scope of the area proposed to be mined 
in the Application in accordance with paragraph 5 herein, The Town agrees not to raise any subject 
matter jurisdictional defense based upon CMA’s failure to e xhaust administrative remedies, and 
CMA agrees not to assert any claim based upon alleged denials of Due Process under the State or 
Federal Constitutions.  
7. Upon execution of this stipulation the TOWN shall agree to discontinue Proceeding

1, without prejudi ce. Should the DEC resume, at any time and under any circumstances, the 
processing of the Application or any revised, modified, supplemental and/or additional application 
to expand CMA’s mine property in the Town , the TOWN shall have the right to challenge such 
processing and any decisions and/or determinations issued as a result thereof in a proceeding or 
action in a Court of competent jurisdiction  within 60 days of notice given it by DEC that such 
processing has resumed. 
8. The Parties expressly agree that, in any such action or proceeding brought by the 
TOWN, including but not limited to a challenge to  the negative declaration pursuant to the State 
Environmental Quality Review Act (“SEQRA”) issued by DEC in conjunction with the 
Application or any revised, modified, supplemental and/or additional application to expand

regard to such action or proceeding based upon service of process, personal jurisdiction and/or the 
timeliness of the commencement of the proceeding or action, but  do not herein waive any other 
defenses available to the m under the CPLR. The Parties agree that all claims pertaining to the 
SEQRA determination by DEC are tolled accordingly, in accord with a separate tolling agreement 
to be entered into by the TOWN and DEC, the terms of which are expressly incorporated herein 
by reference.

executed by counsel for all parties.
