TOLLING AGREEMENT
This Tolling Agreement (the "Agreeme nt") is dated and effective as of March_ . 2025.
by and between the Town of Riverhead ("t he Town") and New York State Department of
Environmental Conservation ("D EC ) .
WHEREAS. on February 19, 2019. CMA Mine LLC ("CMA") the operator of a sand
mine, filed an application with DEC seeking to modify its existing mining permit; and
WHEREAS, on September 29. 2020. DEC issued a "Negative Declaration" under the
State Environmental Quality Review Act, finding that the permit modification would not have
significant environmental impacts; and
WHEREAS, on January 26, 2021, the Town filed a special proceeding under CPLR
article 78, seeking the annulment of the September 2020 Negative Declaration, see Town of
Riverhead v. New YorkState Department of Environmental Conservation, et al.. Index No.
601509/2021 (the "202I Proceeding") : and
WHEREAS, in light of the Court of Appeals' February 2023 decision Town of
Southampton v. DEC, 39 N.Y.3d 201 (2023), in April 2023. DEC formally inquired of the Town
whether the mining activities proposed in CMA's application were within the scope of a prior,
nonconforming use, and the Town subsequently advised DEC, amongst other things. that CMA
had a nonconforming use to mine within the then permitted life of mine area, but had not
established, on the current available records, that CMA had manifested the intention to expand its
mine beyond its current parameters at such time as the use became nonconforming and, therefore,
that it was incumbent upon CMA to make that showing to the Town as a necessary condition
precedent to DEC's continued processing and consideration of the application; and
WHEREAS DEC subsequently ceased processing CMA's modification application; and
9.29.b
Packet Pg. 185
Attachment: 250317 Town DEC stip of discon and tolling FINAL signed by CMA (1)  (2025-308 : Authorizes Special Counsel to Resolve Pending
WHEREAS, to date, DEC has neither resumed processing CMA's February 2019
Modification Application, nor rendered adecision on the February 2019 Modification
Application; and
WHEREAS, on February 23, 2024, the Town filed an Amended Petition in the 2021
Proceeding; and
WHEREAS, in conjunction with the execution of this Tolling Agreement, the Town
stipulates to the discontinuance of the 2021 Proceeding, as set forth in the accompanying
Stipulation of Discontinuance;
NOW, THEREFORE, in consideration of the foregoing. the Town and DEC, through the
respective undersigned counsel, agree as follows:
I. In the event DEC resumes processing CMA's February 2019 Modification
Application and grants (in whole or in part) CMA's February 2019 Modification Application, the
limitations period set forth in CPLR §217, to the extent such provision governs a claim brought
by the Town challenging the September 2020 Negative Declaration, and/or any other applicable
limitations period, shall be tolled until four months after DEC renders its decision on the
February 2019 Modification Application (the "T olled Period") .
2. The persons or entities signing this Agreement warrant and represent that they
have obtained all necessary authorizations to enter into this Agreement, and that they are aware
of no reason why this Agreement is not legally effective.
3. The Parties agree that except as otherwise agreed to in this Agreement, this
Agreement shall not be construed as a waiver or relinquishment of the rights of any party to
make any legal or factual argument raised in the 2021 Proceeding, or in any new action or
proceeding.

Main Street and did submit a site plan for a proposed mixed use residential and retail

consists of a single ﬁve (5) story-60 foot high structure with approximately 3,500 square

the upper four ﬂoors (ﬂoors 2-5) described as: 52 studio units, 80 one bedroom units, 33

(Project). On October 3, 2023, the Town Board granted ﬁnal site plan approval for the

Chapter 231. Fire Prevention 
Article VII. Fire Department Access and Operations 
 
§ 231-24 Interference with Fire Department, Fire Marshal or CEO. 
C.  No person shall reset a fire alarm in a commercial or multifamily building without approval from the Fire 
Chief, Fire Marshal, Fire Department Officer in Charge, or Code Enforcement Official. 
(1)  A sign, approved by the Riverhead Fire Marshal, shall be posted by the fire alarm panel stating that 
the fire alarm shall not be reset without the approval of the Fire Chief as set forth in § 231-24 (C) above. 
(2)  This provision, § 231-24 (C), shall exclude single-and two-family dwellings.

9.33.a
Packet Pg. 250
Attachment: Notice of Public Hearing 231.25 Fire Prevention (Outdoor Fires)  (2025-312 : Publish and Post Public Notice to Amend 231.25
 
 
Chapter 231. Fire Prevention 
Article VIII. Precautions Against Fire 
 
§ 231-25. Outdoor fires. 
A. Permit required. 
(1) No person shall ignite or maintain any outdoor fire, except a fire used exclusively to 
cook food for human consumption, without first having obtained a burn permit from the 
Town Fire Marshal and any other required agency. 
(2) No person shall kindle or maintain an outdoor fire to be unsafe or hazard -producing as 
determined by the Fire Chief, Fire Marshal, State Forest Ranger or state, county or Town 
police officer, who may immediately suspend or revoke any burn permit previously 
issued. 
B. Who may prohibit. The Chief of the Fire Department or the Fire Marshal may prohibit any or 
all bonfires and outdoor r ubbish fires when atmospheric conditions, drought or unfavorable 
weather conditions or local circumstances make such fires hazardous. 
 
A.    No person shall kindle, maintain, authorize or permit any bonfires, recreational fires or open 
burning on or in any street, alley, road, land or public grounds or upon any private lot, unless 
conducted in accordance with this section and with the Building and Fire Code of New York 
State and New York Code Rules and Regulations Title 6 New York State Department of 
Environmental Conservation. Chapter III Part 215.  
Fires that are used to dispose of  flags or religious items that are used in connection with a 
religious ceremony as defined in the Fire Code of New York State shall be considered exempt 
from this subsection upon satisfactory proof and/or testimony.  
(1) Residential Property 
a. No Permit required. 
i. Notwithstanding A (1)(a) above, n o person shall kindle or maintain any 
bonfire on any privately owned property without adhering to the following 
provisions: 
1. No fire shall be kindled or maintained unless it is a minimum of 25 
feet from any building or structure;  
2. No fire shall be left unattended 
3. No fire be kindled  or maintained if the prevailing wind exceeds a 
velocity of 15 miles per hour 
4. No fire shall be kindled or maintained as to create or cause to be 
created any noxious or offensive odor or smoke as to be hazard -
producing 
9.33.b
Packet Pg. 251
Attachment: 231.25 Outdoor Fires  (2025-312 : Publish and Post Public Notice to Amend 231.25  (Outdoor Fires))
 
 
5. No fire shall be kindled or maintained  unless adequate provisions 
are made to prevent the spread of fire 
6. No fire shall be kindled or maintained without an appropriate fire 
extinguishing source   
7. No fire shall be kindled or maintained unless in an approved above-
ground fire pit or a permanent in-ground fire pit 
8. No fire shall be kindled or maintained with any combustible fuels 
other than dry, plain, untreated wood. All other fuels are considered 
unapproved combustibles fuels. 
 
This shall in no way be construed as applicable to barbeque grills, outdoor 
fireplaces or gas-fueled fire pits 
(2) Commercial Property 
a. Permit required 
i. No person shall kindle or maintain any bonfire fire without first having 
obtained a burn permit from the Town of Riverhead Fire Marshal’s Office. 
(3) Town of Riverhead Property 
a. Permit Required  
i. No person shall kindle of maintain any bonfire on Town of Riverhead 
property without first having obtained a bonfire permit from the Town of 
Riverhead Fire Marshal’s Office. 
 
B.   No person shall kindle or maintain any outdoor fire determined to be unsafe or hazard-producing 
as set forth in § 231-25 and as determined by the Fire Chief, Fire Marshal, Code Enforcement 
Officer and/or State Forest Ranger or state, county or town police officer and such official may 
immediately suspend or revoke any permit previously issued. 
 
C.   Who may prohibit. The Fire Chief or Fire Marshal, may prohibit any or all bonfires and outdoor 
fires or open burning when atmospheric conditions, drought or  other unfavorable weather 
conditions or local circumstances make such fires hazardous. 
 
 
Underline represents addition(s) 
Strikethrough represents deletion(s)

Attachment: 231.25 Outdoor Fires  (2025-312 : Publish and Post Public Notice to Amend 231.25  (Outdoor Fires))

TB Resolution 2025-313 
 
AUTHORIZE TOWN CLERK TO PUBLISH AND POST PUBLIC NOTICE TO 
CONSIDER A LOCAL LAW TO AMEND CHAPTER 231 OF THE RIVERHEAD TOWN

9.34.a
Packet Pg. 255
Attachment: Notice of Public Hearing 231.38 Fire Prevention (Flammable Liquids Gas Pumps)  (2025-313 : Publish and Post Public Notice to
Chapter 231. Fire Prevention 
Article XIV. Flammable and Combustible Liquids 
§ 231-38. Applicability. 
A. This article shall apply to the storage, handling and use of flammable liquids as defined in 
Article II, except that it shall not apply to the transportation of flammable liquids when in 
conformity with regulations of th e Federal and State Departments of Transportation or 
regulations lawfully on file with and approved by the Federal and State Departments of 
Transportation. 
 
B. New and existing installations of flammable motor fuel dispensing systems shall have and 
maintain an automatic fire-extinguishing system using an extinguishing agent suitable for 
petroleum fires and installed in accordance with NFPA 17 and their listings, and UL 1254 
Standard for Pre -Engineered Dry Chemical Extinguishing systems. The fire protection 
system shall be connected to the fire alarm system, if provided, in accordance with the 
requirements of NFPA 72. 
 
C. The proposed Article XIV §231-38(B) is enacted pursuant to Municipal Home Rule Law 
§ 10(1)(ii)(a)(11), (12) and (14);

Strikethrough represents deletion(s)

9.35.a
Packet Pg. 259
Attachment: Notice of Public Hearing 231.14 Fire Prevention Assistance to Authorized Agencies (Battery Storage Spills)  (2025-314 : Publish
Chapter 231. Fire Prevention 
Article IV. Mitigation of Hazardous Condition or 
Occurrence 
 
§ 231-14 Assistance to authorized agencies; reimbursement of expenses 
 
C. The person or entity responsible for the spill, discharge or other release of any hazardous 
material that creates any hazardous condition or occurrence as described in § 231-14 above 
shall be responsible to reimburse the Town for all expenses incurred by the Town for the 
mitigation and investigation of the hazardous condition or occurrence. This section shall 
not apply to accidental spills or releases of home heating oil, residential swimming pool 
treatments or similar materials within or on the premises of owner-occupied single-family 
dwellings, unless such spill or release was due to a negligent or intentional act. This section 
shall apply to the use or storage of lithium-ion batteries and battery installations that 
contain flammable electrolytes and hazardous devices i.e. fireproof and heat resistant fire 
extinguisher blanket. 
 
 
Underline represents addition(s) 
Strikethrough represents deletion(s)

9.36.a
Packet Pg. 263
Attachment: Notice of Public Hearing 231.7 Fire Prevention Definitions  (2025-315 : Publish and Post Public Notice to Amend  Chapter 231.7 Fire
 
 
Chapter 231. Fire Prevention 
Article II. Terminology 
 
§ 231-7. Definitions. 
Unless otherwise expressly stated, the following terms shall, for the purpose of this chapter, have 
the meanings indicated in this section: 
 
Bonfire/Recreational Fire - An outdoor fire burning wood materials where the fuel being burned 
is not contained in an outdoor fireplace or barbecue grill and has a total fuel area of 30 inches or 
less in diameter and 24 inches or less in hei ght from natural grade for pleasure, religious, 
ceremonial, cooking, warmth or similar purposes. 
 
Burn Permit – A permit obtained from the Town of Riverhead Fire Marshal’s Office for opening 
burning of agricultural materials associated with a commercial operation. 
 
Bonfire Permit – A permit obtained from the Town of Riverhead Fire Marshal’s Office for use of 
a firepit on Town Property or Commercial Property. 
 
Fire Extinguishing Source – A method of extinguishing an outdoor fire to include a fire 
extinguisher, water can, water bucket or garden hose. 
 
Unapproved Combustible Fuels – Combustible fuels that are not permitted to be burned in outdoor 
fires to include: trash or garbage; plastic, glass or metal items (tin and aluminum cans); pressure -
treated lumber or plywood; painted or stained wood products; construction debris.  
 
Hazardous Materials (HAZMAT) - Substances that can be a threat to the environment or human 
health. These substances can be solids, liquids, or gases, and include but not limited  to: explosives, 
thermal decomposition of batteries ie. thermal runaway, flammable liquids and solids, combustible 
liquids, various types of gas, heavy metals, such as lead, mercury, cadmium, arsenic, and chromium,  
volatile organic compounds (VOCs), such as benzene, toluene, and ethylbenzene, semi volatile 
organic compounds (SVOCs), such as phenols and other components of creosote and coal and 
radioactive materials.  
 
Underline represents addition(s) 
Strikethrough represents deletion(s)

9.39
Packet Pg. 278
§ 231-66 Penalties for offenses; notice of violation. 
A. Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of this chapter or fail to comply with the 
provisions thereof, or who shall violate or fail to comply with any order made thereunder, except 
for § 231-55 shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, punishable by a fine of not less than $250 nor 
more than $2,500 or by imprisonment for not more than 15 days, or by both such fine and 
imprisonment. 
B. The imposition of a penalty for any violation shall not excuse the violation or allow it to 
continue, and all such persons shall be required to correct or remedy such violations or defects 
within a reasonable time, and when not otherwise specified, a separate offense shall be deemed 
committed for each day that the prohibited conditions are maintained following receipt of a 
notice from the Fire Marshal or CEO identifying the violation and requiring its correction. Said 
notice shall be mailed to the owner, at his or her mailing address as listed on the Town's most 
recent tax roll, by certified mail, return-receipt requested. 
C. A civil penalty in the amount of $500 shall be imposed for each violation of Article V of this 
chapter. 
D. Any person who shall violate § 231-55 of this chapter shall be guilty of a violation level 
offense, punishable by a fine of not less than $250 nor more than $2,500 or by 
imprisonment for not more than 15 days, or by both such fine and imprisonment. 
 
 
 
9.39.a
Packet Pg. 279

TOWN OF RIVERHEAD  
NOTICE OF PUBLIC HEARING  
 
 PLEASE TAKE NOTICE that a public hearing will be held before the Town Board of the 
Town of Riverhead at Riverhead Town Hall, 4 West Second Street, Riverhead, New York, on the 
6th day of May, 2025 at or about 2:25 p.m. to amend Chapter 231 of the Riverhead Town 
Code titled “Fire Prevention”, Section 66 thereof titled, “Penalties for Offenses”. 
 
The intent of the proposed legislation is to reduce § 231-55 from a violation level offense 
to a misdemeanor level offense to be reflected in the Penalties section of §231-66 
 
 A copy of the entire text of the proposed local law and the provisions of the existing law to 
be amended may be reviewed at the Office of the Town Clerk, 4 West Second Street, Riverhead, 
New York 11901, between the hours of 8:30 a.m. and 4:30 p.m., Monday through Friday and can 
be accessed on the Town of Riverhead website at: www.townofriverheadny.gov under the Agenda

TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
Notice of Adoption 
 
 PLEASE TAKE NOTICE, that the Town Board of the Town of Riverhead, adopted 
a Local Law to Amend Chapter 301 Zoning and Land Development, Part 3 Supplementary 
Use Regulations, Article XLVIII Signs, §301-254 H. Zoning Use Districts. The intent of the 
proposed legislation is to implement recommendations of the 2024 Comprehensive Plan 
Update to remove references to the Industrial A, B, and C Zoning Use Districts and include 
the Calverton Industrial and Light Industrial Zoning Use Districts. 
A copy of the entire text of the adopted local law and the provisions of the existing 
law to be amended may be reviewed at the Office of the Town Clerk, 4 W Second Street, 
Riverhead, New York 11901, between the hours of 8:3 0 a.m. and 4:30 p.m., Monday 
through Friday and can be accessed on the Town of Riverhead website at:

Board Meeting.

§ 301-254. Zoning use district regulations.  
H. CI, and LI. In the Calverton Industrial (CI) and Light Industrial (LI) Zoning Use Districts, all 
signs are permitted, with the exception of:  
(1) Internally illuminated (including neon) signs, except in windows.  
(2) Electronic time/temperature display.  
(3) Roof signs (except on mansard roof(s).

TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-320 
 
ADOPTS LOCAL LAW TO AMEND CHAPTER 301 ZONING AND LAND 
DEVELOPMENT, PART 3 SUPPLEMENTARY USE REGULATIONS, ARTICLE LII 
COMMERCIAL SOLAR ENERGY PRODUCTION SYSTEMS,  §301-281 PURPOSE; 
PERMITTED DISTRICTS; DEFINITIONS PURSUANT TO THE RECOMMENDATIONS 
OF THE 2024 COMPREHENSIVE PLAN UPDATE 
 
Councilman Rothwell offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilman Kern 
 
WHEREAS, by Resolution No. 2024 -760 dated September 4, 2024, The Town 
Board of the Town of Riverhead issued a Findings Statement and adopted the Town of 
Riverhead 2024 Comprehensive Plan Update; and 
 
WHEREAS, by Resolution No. 2025 -193 the Town Clerk was authorized to 
publish and post a public notice to hear all interested p ersons to consider a local law to 
amend Chapter 301 Zoning and Land Development, Part 3 Supplementary Use 
Regulations, Article LII Commercial Solar Energy Production Systems,  §301-281 
Purpose; Permitted Districts,  of the Code of the Town of Riverhead (“Riv erhead Town 
Code”); and 
 
WHEREAS, a public hearing was held on the 4 th day of March 2025 at 2:00 
o'clock p.m. at the Riverhead Town Hall, 4 W Second Street Riverhead, New York, the 
date, time and place specified in said public notice, and all persons wishi ng to be heard 
were heard, with said hearing closed with a 10-day written comment period; and 
 
WHEREAS, by letter dated March 25, 2025 the Suffolk County Planning 
Commission (SCPC) provided the following Comments:  
  
“Pursuant to the requirements of Sectio ns A 14 -14 to A 14 -25 of the Suffolk 
County Administrative Code, the above referenced application which has been 
submitted to the Suffolk County Planning Commission is considered to be a 
matter for local determination as there is no apparent significant co unty-wide or 
inter-community impact(s). A decision of local determination should not be 
construed as either an approval or disapproval;” and 
 
WHEREAS, at this time the Town Board desires to implement the 
recommendations of the 2024 Comprehensive Plan Update; and  
 
WHEREAS, the proposed amendments are a Type I action pursuant to SEQRA 
(NYCRR 617.4 b (2)); and 
 
WHEREAS, the Riverhead Planning Department Staff, on behalf of the Town 
Board Has completed Part 1 of the Full Environmental Assessment Form (FEAF) da ted 
January 31, 2025 as well as Parts 2 and 3 of the SEAF dated April 1, 2025; and

of the Code of the Town of Riverhead (“Riverhead Town Code”) as the proposed action 
is not likely to result in any significant adverse environmental impacts; and be it further

TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
Notice of Adoption 
 
 PLEASE TAKE NOTICE, that the Town Board of the Town of Riverhead, adopted 
a Local Law to Amend Chapter 301 Zoning and Land Development, Part 3 Supplementary 
Use Regulations, Article LII Commercial Solar Energy Production Systems, §301-281 B. & C. 
Purposes; permitted districts; definitions. The intent of the proposed legislation is to implement 
recommendations of the 2024 Comprehensive Plan Update to remove references to the 
Industrial A, Industrial B, and Industrial C Zoning Use Districts and include Calverton Industrial 
and Light Industrial Zoning Use Districts. 
A copy of the entire text of the adopted local law and the provisions of the existing 
law to be amended may be reviewed at the Office of the Town Clerk, 4 W Second Street, 
Riverhead, New York 11901, between the hours of 8:30 a.m. and 4:30 p.m., Monday 
through Friday and can be accessed on the Town of Riverhead website at: 
www.townofriverheadny.gov under the Agenda and Minutes for the April 1, 2025  Town 
Board Meeting.  
Dated:  Riverhead, New York 
   April 1, 2025 
 
 
BY ORDER OF THE TOWN BOARD 
OF THE TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
JAMES M. WOOTEN, TOWN CLERK 
 
9.41.a
Packet Pg. 294
Attachment: Notice of Adoption to Amend Chapter 301 Zoning and Land Development, Part 3 Supplementary Use Regulations, Article LII
Downloaded from https://ecode360.com/RI0508 on 2025-01-13 
 
 
§ 301-281. Purpose; permitted districts; definitions.  
A. It is the intention of the Town Board of the Town of Riverhead, as part of its goal to limit 
dependence on imported fossil energy and decrease greenhouse gas emissions, to permit 
commercial solar energy production systems in the industrial zoning use districts to minimize 
impacts to residents and scenic viewsheds important to the community. 
B. Commercial solar energy production systems shall be allowed with special permit approval 
by the Town Board in the Calverton Industrial (CI) and the Planned Industrial Park (PIP) 
District. 
C. Commercial solar energy production systems shall be allowed with special permit approval 
by the Town Board in the Light Industrial (LI) Zoning Use District that is located within the 
zip code boundary of Calverton. 
D. Definitions. As used in this section, the following terms shall have the meanings indicated: 
LOT COVERAGE — The lot coverage shall include the total square footage of the perimeter 
of all of the solar panels, inclusive of all interior spaces between the panels, in addition to 
driveways and service roads (paved or stone), and all accessory equipment, buildings and 
structures.

Instructions for Completing Part 1 
Part 1 is to be completed by the applicant or project sponsor.  Responses become part of the application for approval or funding, 
are subject to public review, and may be subject to further verification. 
Complete Part 1 based on information currently available.  If additional research or investigation would be needed to fully respond to 
any item, please answer as thoroughly as possible based on current information; indicate whether missing information does not exist, 
or is not reasonably available to the sponsor; and, when possible, generally describe work or studies which would be necessary to 
update or fully develop that information. 
Applicants/sponsors must complete all items in Sections A & B.  In Sections C, D & E, most items contain an initial question that 
must be answered either “Yes” or “No”. If the answer to the initial question is “Yes”, complete the sub-questions that follow.  If the 
answer to the initial question is “No”, proceed to the next question. Section F allows the project sponsor to identify and attach any 
additional information.  Section G requires the name and signature of the applicant or project sponsor to verify that the information 
contained in Part 1is accurate and complete.

Full Environmental Assessment Form 
Part 2 - Identification of Potential Project Impacts 
Part 2 is to be completed by the lead agency.  Part 2 is designed to help the lead agency inventory all potential resources that could 
be affected by a proposed project or action.  We recognize that the lead agency=s reviewer(s) will not necessarily be environmental 
professionals.  So, the questions are designed to walk a reviewer through the assessment process by providing a series of questions that 
can be answered using the information found in Part 1.  To further assist the lead agency in completing Part 2, the form identifies the 
most relevant questions in Part 1 that will provide the information needed to answer the Part 2 question.  When Part 2 is completed, the 
lead agency will have identified the relevant environmental areas that may be impacted by the proposed activity.   
If the lead agency is a state agency and the action is in any Coastal Area, complete the Coastal Assessment Form before proceeding 
with this assessment. 
Tips for completing Part 2: 
• Review all of the information provided in Part 1.
• Review any application, maps, supporting materials and the Full EAF Workbook.
• Answer each of the 18 questions in Part 2.
• If you answer “Yes” to a numbered question, please complete all the questions that follow in that section.
• If you answer “No” to a numbered question, move on to the next numbered question.
• Check appropriate column to indicate the anticipated size of the impact.
• Proposed projects that would exceed a numeric threshold contained in a question should result in the reviewing agency
checking the box “Moderate to large impact may occur.”
• The reviewer is not expected to be an expert in environmental analysis.
• If you are not sure or undecided about the size of an impact, it may help to review the sub-questions for the general
question and consult the workbook.
• When answering a question consider all components of the proposed activity, that is, the Awhole action@.
• Consider the possibility for long-term and cumulative impacts as well as direct impacts.
• Answer the question in a reasonable manner considering the scale and context of the project.

Full Environmental Assessment Form 
Part 3 - Evaluation of the Magnitude and Importance of Project Impacts 
and  
Determination of Significance 
Part 3 provides the reasons in support of the determination of significance.  The lead agency must complete Part 3 for every question 
in Part 2 where the impact has been identified as potentially moderate to large or where there is a need to explain why a particular 
element of the proposed action will not, or may, result in a significant adverse environmental impact. 
Based on the analysis in Part 
3, the lead agency must decide whether to require an environmental impact statement to further assess 
the proposed action or whether available information is sufficient for the lead agency to conclude that the proposed action will not 
have a significant adverse environmental impact.  By completing the certification on the next page, the lead agency can complete its 
determination of significance. 
Reasons Supporting This Determination: 
To com
plete this section: 
• Identify the impact based on the Part 2 responses and describe its magnitude.  Magnitude considers factors such as severity,
size or extent of an impact.
• Assess th
e importance of the impact.  Importance relates to the geographic scope, duration, probability of the impact
occurring, number of people affected by the impact and any additional environmental consequences if the impact were to
occur.
• The as
sessment should take into consideration any design element or project changes.
• Repeat this process for each Part 2 question where the impact has been identified as potentially moderate to large or where
there is a need to explain why a particular element of the proposed action will not, or may, result in a significant adverse
environmental impact.
• Provide the reason(s) why the impact may, or will not, result in a significant adverse environmental impact
• For Conditional Negative Declarations identify the specific condition(s) imposed that will modify the proposed action so that
no significant adverse environmental impacts will result.
• Attach additional sheets, as needed.
Determination of Significance - Type 1 and Unlisted Actions

Upon review of the information recorded on this EAF, as noted, plus this additional support information 
and consi
dering both the magnitude and importance of each identified potential impact, it is the conclusion of the 
 as lead agency that: 
  A. 
This project will result in no significant adverse impacts on the environment, and, therefore, an environmental impact 
statement need not be prepared.  Accordingly, this negative declaration is issued. 
 B. Alth
ough this project could have a significant adverse impact on the environment, that impact will be avoided or 
substantially mitigated because of the following conditions which will be required by the lead agency: 
There will, therefore, be no significant adverse impacts from the project as conditioned, and, therefore, this conditioned negative 
declaration is issued.  A conditioned negative declaration may be used only for UNLISTED actions (see 6 NYCRR 617.7(d)). 
 C. This Project may result in one or more sig nificant adverse impacts on the environment, and an environmental impact 
statement must be prepared to further assess the impact(s) and possible mitigation and to explore alternatives to avoid or reduce those 
impacts.  Accordingly, this positive declaration is issued.

04.01.2025 ADOPTED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-321 
 
ADOPTS LOCAL LAW TO AMEND CHAPTER 301 ZONING AND LAND 
DEVELOPMENT, PART 3 SUPPLEMENTARY USE REGULATIONS, ARTICLE LI 
WIRELESS COMMUNICATIONS TOWERS, ANTENNAS AND SATELLITE EARTH 
STATIONS, §301-274 PERMIT REQUIRED; APPLICABILITY, PURSUANT TO THE 
RECOMMENDATIONS OF THE 2024 COMPREHENSIVE PLAN UPDATE 
 
Councilman Kern offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilwoman Merrifield 
 
WHEREAS, by Resolution No. 2024 -760 dated September  4, 2024, The Town 
Board of the Town of Riverhead issued a Findings Statement and adopted the Town of 
Riverhead 2024 Comprehensive Plan Update; and 
 
WHEREAS, by Resolution No. 2025 -194 the Town Clerk was authorized to 
publish and post a public notice to he ar all interested persons to consider a local law to 
amend Chapter 301 Zoning and Land Development, Part 3 Supplementary Use 
Regulations, Article LI Wireless Communications Towers, Antennas and Satellite Earth 
Stations, §301-274 Permit required; applicabil ity, of the Code of the Town of Riverhead 
(“Riverhead Town Code”); and 
 
WHEREAS, a public hearing was held on the 4 th day of March 2025 at 2:00 
o'clock p.m. at the Riverhead Town Hall, 4 W Second Street Riverhead, New York, the 
date, time and place specified in said public notice, and all persons wishing to be heard 
were heard, with said hearing closed with a 10-day written comment period; and 
 
WHEREAS, by letter dated March 25, 2025 the Suffolk County Planning 
Commission (SCPC) provided the following Comments:  
  
“Pursuant to the requirements of Sections A 14 -14 to A 14 -25 of the Suffolk 
County Administrative Code, the above referenced application which has been 
submitted to the Suffolk County Planning Commission is considered to be a 
matter for local deter mination as there is no apparent significant county -wide or 
inter-community impact(s). A decision of local determination should not be 
construed as either an approval or disapproval;” and 
 
WHEREAS, at this time the Town Board desires to implement the 
recommendations of the 2024 Comprehensive Plan Update; and  
 
WHEREAS, the proposed amendments are a Type I action pursuant to SEQRA 
(NYCRR 617.4 b (2)); and 
 
WHEREAS, the Riverhead Planning Department Staff, on behalf of the Town 
Board Has completed Part 1 of t he Full Environmental Assessment Form (FEAF) dated 
January 31, 2025 as well as Parts 2 and 3 of the SEAF dated April 1, 2025; and

RESOLVED, that the Riverhead Town Board hereby assumes Lead Agency and 
issues a Negative Declaration pursuant to SEQRA, for t he Local Law to amend Chapter 
301 Zoning and Land Development, Part 3 Supplementary Use Regulations, Article LI 
Wireless Communications Towers, Antennas and Satellite Earth Stations, §301 -274 
Permit required; applicability,  of the Code of the Town of River head (“Riverhead Town 
Code”) as the proposed action is not likely to result in any significant adverse 
environmental impacts; and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that the local law to amend Chapter 301 Zoning and Land 
Development, Part 3 Supplementary Use Regulat ions, Article LI Wireless 
Communications Towers, Antennas and Satellite Earth Stations, §301 -274 Permit 
required; applicability, of the Code of the Town of Riverhead (“Riverhead Town Code”) 
is hereby adopted as specified in the attached notice of adoption; and be it further 
 
 RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk be and is hereby directed to forward a copy of 
this resolution to Planning Department and the Office of the Town Attorney; and be it 
further 
 
RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of 
this resolution from the electronic storage device and, if needed, a certified copy of 
same may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk.   
 
THE VOTE

MOVER: Robert Kern, Councilman 
SECONDER: Denise Merrifield, Councilwoman 
AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
Notice of Adoption 
 
 PLEASE TAKE NOTICE, that the Town Board of the Town of Riverhead, adopted 
a Local Law to Amend Chapter 301 Zoning and Land Development, Part 3 Supplementary 
Use Regulations, Article LI Wireless Communications Tower, Antennas, and Satellite Earth 
Stations, §301-274 Permit Requirement; Applicability. The intent of the proposed legislation 
is to implement recommendations of the 2024 Comprehensive Plan Update to remove 
references to the Industrial A and Industrial C Zoning Use Districts and include the Calverton 
Industrial and Light Industrial Zoning Use Districts.  
A copy of the entire text of the adopted local law and the provisions of the existing 
law to be amended may be reviewed at the Office of the Town Clerk, 4 W Second Street, 
Riverhead, New York 11901, between the hours of 8:30 a.m. and 4:30 p.m., Monday 
through Friday and can be accessed on the Town of Riverhead website at: 
www.townofriverheadny.gov under the Agenda and Minutes for the April 1, 2025  Town 
Board Meeting.  
Dated:  Riverhead, New York 
   April 1, 2025 
 
 
BY ORDER OF THE TOWN BOARD 
OF THE TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
JAMES M. WOOTEN, TOWN CLERK 
 
9.42.a
Packet Pg. 324
Attachment: Notice of Adoption to Amend Chapter 301 Zoning and Land Development, Part 3 Supplementary Use Regulations, Article LI
 
 
§ 301-274. Permit required; applicability. 
A. No telecommunications tower or satellite earth station shall hereafter be used, erected, moved, 
reconstructed, changed, altered or modified to serve as a telecommunications tower or  
satellite earth station without the issuance of a special use permit(s) by the Town Board in 
conformity with the requirements of this article. 
B. Towers shall be permitted by special permit only in the following zoning use districts: APZ, 
PIP, PRP, RFC, DRC, SC, BC, CRC, CI, LI, RLC, and TRC, but shall not be permitted in 
whole or in part on any property used for residential purposes. 
C. Satellite earth stations shall by permitted by special permit only in the CI, LI, PIP and PD 
Zoning use districts, and sha ll not be permitted in whole or in part on any property used for 
residential purposes. 
D. New towers, antennas and satellite earth stations. All new towers, antennas and satellite earth 
stations in the Town shall be subject to these regulations, except as oth erwise provided 
hereinbelow. 
E. Exceptions. The requirements set forth in this article shall not be applicable to: 
(1) Amateur radio operators' antennas and/or towers not exceeding 50 feet in height, which 
are owned and operated by a federally licensed amateur radio operator and which are 
located upon property that is the principal place of business or primary residence of the 
amateur radio operator. 
(2) Preexisting towers or antennas. 
(3) Residential satellite earth stations less than or equal to two meters in diameter.

Part 1 - Project and Setting 
Instructions for Completing Part 1 
Part 1 is to be completed by the applicant or project sponsor.  Responses become part of the application for approval or funding, 
are subject to public review, and may be subject to further verification. 
Complete Part 1 based on information currently available.  If additional research or investigation would be needed to fully respond to 
any item, please answer as thoroughly as possible based on current information; indicate whether missing information does not exist, 
or is not reasonably available to the sponsor; and, when possible, generally describe work or studies which would be necessary to 
update or fully develop that information. 
Applicants/sponsors must complete all items in Sections A & B.  In Sections C, D & E, most items contain an initial question that 
must be answered either “Yes” or “No”. If the answer to the initial question is “Yes”, complete the sub-questions that follow.  If the 
answer to the initial question is “No”, proceed to the next question. Section F allows the project sponsor to identify and attach any 
additional information.  Section G requires the name and signature of the applicant or project sponsor to verify that the information 
contained in Part 1is accurate and complete.

Full Environmental Assessment Form 
Part 2 - Identification of Potential Project Impacts 
Part 2 is to be completed by the lead agency.  Part 2 is designed to help the lead agency inventory all potential resources that could 
be affected by a proposed project or action.  We recognize that the lead agency=s reviewer(s) will not necessarily be environmental 
professionals.  So, the questions are designed to walk a reviewer through the assessment process by providing a series of questions that 
can be answered using the information found in Part 1.  To further assist the lead agency in completing Part 2, the form identifies the 
most relevant questions in Part 1 that will provide the information needed to answer the Part 2 question.  When Part 2 is completed, the 
lead agency will have identified the relevant environmental areas that may be impacted by the proposed activity.   
If the lead agency is a state agency and the action is in any Coastal Area, complete the Coastal Assessment Form before proceeding 
with this assessment. 
Tips for completing Part 2: 
• Review all of the information provided in Part 1.
• Review any application, maps, supporting materials and the Full EAF Workbook.
• Answer each of the 18 questions in Part 2.
• If you answer “Yes” to a numbered question, please complete all the questions that follow in that section.
• If you answer “No” to a numbered question, move on to the next numbered question.
• Check appropriate column to indicate the anticipated size of the impact.
• Proposed projects that would exceed a numeric threshold contained in a question should result in the reviewing agency
checking the box “Moderate to large impact may occur.”
• The reviewer is not expected to be an expert in environmental analysis.
• If you are not sure or undecided about the size of an impact, it may help to review the sub-questions for the general
question and consult the workbook.
• When answering a question consider all components of the proposed activity, that is, the Awhole action@.
• Consider the possibility for long-term and cumulative impacts as well as direct impacts.
• Answer the question in a reasonable manner considering the scale and context of the project.

Full Environmental Assessment Form 
Part 3 - Evaluation of the Magnitude and Importance of Project Impacts 
and  
Determination of Significance 
Part 3 provides the reasons in support of the determination of significance.  The lead agency must complete Part 3 for every question 
in Part 2 where the impact has been identified as potentially moderate to large or where there is a need to explain why a particular 
element of the proposed action will not, or may, result in a significant adverse environmental impact. 
Based on the analysis in Part 
3, the lead agency must decide whether to require an environmental impact statement to further assess 
the proposed action or whether available information is sufficient for the lead agency to conclude that the proposed action will not 
have a significant adverse environmental impact.  By completing the certification on the next page, the lead agency can complete its 
determination of significance. 
Reasons Supporting This Determination: 
To com
plete this section: 
• Identify the impact based on the Part 2 responses and describe its magnitude.  Magnitude considers factors such as severity,
size or extent of an impact.
• Assess th
e importance of the impact.  Importance relates to the geographic scope, duration, probability of the impact
occurring, number of people affected by the impact and any additional environmental consequences if the impact were to
occur.
• The as
sessment should take into consideration any design element or project changes.
• Repeat this process for each Part 2 question where the impact has been identified as potentially moderate to large or where
there is a need to explain why a particular element of the proposed action will not, or may, result in a significant adverse
environmental impact.
• Provide the reason(s) why the impact may, or will not, result in a significant adverse environmental impact
• For Conditional Negative Declarations identify the specific condition(s) imposed that will modify the proposed action so that
no significant adverse environmental impacts will result.
• Attach additional sheets, as needed.
Determination of Significance - Type 1 and Unlisted Actions 
SEQR Status:    Type 1   Unlisted

of EAF completed for this Project:   Part 1   Part 2   Part 3

Upon review of the information recorded on this EAF, as noted, plus this additional support information 
and consi
dering both the magnitude and importance of each identified potential impact, it is the conclusion of the 
 as lead agency that: 
  A. 
This project will result in no significant adverse impacts on the environment, and, therefore, an environmental impact 
statement need not be prepared.  Accordingly, this negative declaration is issued. 
 B. Alth
ough this project could have a significant adverse impact on the environment, that impact will be avoided or 
substantially mitigated because of the following conditions which will be required by the lead agency: 
There will, therefore, be no significant adverse impacts from the project as conditioned, and, therefore, this conditioned negative 
declaration is issued.  A conditioned negative declaration may be used only for UNLISTED actions (see 6 NYCRR 617.7(d)). 
 C. This Project may result in one or more sig nificant adverse impacts on the environment, and an environmental impact 
statement must be prepared to further assess the impact(s) and possible mitigation and to explore alternatives to avoid or reduce those 
impacts.  Accordingly, this positive declaration is issued.

04.01.2025 ADOPTED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-322 
 
ADOPTS LOCAL LAW TO AMEND TOWN CODE ARTICLE XLVIII: SIGNS 
 
Councilwoman Merrifield offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilwoman Waski 
 
WHEREAS, by Resolution No. 2025 -198, dated February 19, 2025, the Town 
Clerk was authorized to publish and post a public notice to consider a local law to 
amend Riverhead Town Code Article XLVIII entitled Signs; and  
 
WHEREAS, a public hearing was held on March 4, 2025 at 2:00 o’clock p. m. at 
Riverhead Town Hall, 4 W. 2nd Street, Riverhead, NY, the date, time and place specified 
in said public notice, at which time all persons wishing to be heard were afforded an 
opportunity to speak on the matter; and  
 
WHEREAS, the public hearing was cl osed at the March 4 th, 2025 meeting, with 
the record being left open for the submission of written comments until 4:30 p.m. on 
March 14th, 2025; and  
 
 WHERAS, the proposed code amendment is an Unlisted action pursuant to 
SEQRA, with coordinated review being optional and not recommended; and  
 
 WHEREAS, in a letter dated March 25, 2025, the Suffolk County Planning 
commission provide the following comments: 
 
“Pursuant to the requirements of Sections A14 -14 to A 14 -25 of the Suffolk 
County Administrative Code , the above referenced application which has been 
submitted to the Suffolk County Planning Commission is considered to be a 
matter for local determination as there is no apparent significant county-wide or 
inter-community impact(s).  A decision of local de termination should not be 
construed as either an approval or disapproval;” and 
 
 WHEREAS, the Planning Department has prepared a Short Environmental 
Assessment Form Part 1, dated March 12, 2025, as well as SEAF Parts 2 and 3, dated 
March 26, 2025.  Now, therefore be it 
 
 RESOLVED¸ that the Riverhead Town Board hereby issues a Negative 
Declaration pursuant to SEQRA, as the proposed code amendment is not expected to 
have a significant negative environmental impact; and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that the local law to Amend Town Code Article XLVIII entitled 
Signs,  hereby adopted as specified in the attached notice of adoption; and be it further 
 
9.43
Packet Pg. 351
 RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk be and is hereby directed to forward a copy of 
this resolution to Planning Department and the Office of the Town Attorney; and be it 
further 
  
RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of 
this resolution from the electronic storage device and, if needed, a certified copy of 
same may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk.    
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Denise Merrifield, Councilwoman 
SECONDER: Joann Waski, Councilwoman 
AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
Notice of Adoption 
 
 PLEASE TAKE NOTICE, that the Town Board of the Town of Riverhead, adopted 
a Local Law to Amend Article XLVIII of the Riverhead Town Code entitled Signs.    
A copy of the entire text of the adopted local law and the provisions of the existing 
law to be amended may be reviewed at the Office of the Town Clerk, 4 W Second Street, 
Riverhead, New York 11901, between the hours of 8:30 a.m. and 4:30 p.m., Monday 
through Friday and can be accessed on the Town of Riverhead website at: 
www.townofriverheadny.gov
 under the Agenda Packet for the March 4 th, 2025 Town 
Board Meeting.  
Dated:  Riverhead, New York 
   April 1, 2025  
 
 
BY ORDER OF THE TOWN BOARD 
OF THE TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
JAMES M. WOOTEN, TOWN CLERK

Attachment: 301-255.1 Governmental Authorities Sign Amendment Notice of Adoption  (2025-322 : Adopts Local Law to Amend Town Code
Town of Riverhead, NY 
§ 301-255.1 
Downloaded from https://ecode360.com/RI0508 on 2024-12-11 
 
 
§ 301-255.1. Miscellaneous Provisions 
A. Signs erected by governmental authorities and/or related political subdivisions, excluding signs 
erected pursuant to and in discharge of any governmental function, law or regulation, shall 
comply with this chapter unless otherwise exempt under law or specifically waived by the 
Town Board, upon a recommendation from the Planning Department.  
 
- Underscores represent additions. 
- Strikethroughs represent deletions.

TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-323 
 
ADOPTS LOCAL LAW TO AMEND CHAPTER 301 ZONING AND LAND 
DEVELOPMENT, PART 3 SUPPLEMENTARY USE REGULATIONS, ARTICLE LIID 
BATTERY ENERGY STORAGE SYSTEMS , §301-283.31 REQUIREMENTS FOR 
TIER 2 BATTERY ENERGY STORAGE SYSTEMS PURSUANT TO THE 
RECOMMENDATIONS OF THE 2024 COMPREHENSIVE PLAN UPDATE 
 
Councilwoman Waski offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilman Rothwell 
 
WHEREAS, by Resolution No. 2024 -760 dated September 4, 2024, T he Town 
Board of the Town of Riverhead issued a Findings Statement and adopted the Town of 
Riverhead 2024 Comprehensive Plan Update; and 
 
WHEREAS, by Resolution No. 2025 -193 the Town Clerk was authorized to 
publish and post a public notice to hear all inte rested persons to consider a local law to 
amend Chapter 301 Zoning and Land Development, Article LIID Battery Energy Storage 
Systems, §301-283.31 Requirements for Tier 2 Battery Energy Storage Systems , of the 
Code of the Town of Riverhead (“Riverhead Town Code”); and 
 
WHEREAS, a public hearing was held on the 4 th day of March 2025 at 2:00 
o'clock p.m. at the Riverhead Town Hall, 4 W Second Street Riverhead, New York, the 
date, time and place specified in said public notice, and all persons wishing to be hea rd 
were heard, with said hearing closed with a 10-day written comment period; and 
 
WHEREAS, by letter dated March 25, 2025 the Suffolk County Planning 
Commission (SCPC) provided the following Comments:  
  
“Pursuant to the requirements of Sections A 14 -14 t o A 14 -25 of the Suffolk 
County Administrative Code, the above referenced application which has been 
submitted to the Suffolk County Planning Commission is considered to be a 
matter for local determination as there is no apparent significant county -wide or 
inter-community impact(s). A decision of local determination should not be 
construed as either an approval or disapproval;” and 
 
WHEREAS, at this time the Town Board desires to implement the 
recommendations of the 2024 Comprehensive Plan Update; and  
 
WHEREAS, the proposed amendments are a Type I action pursuant to SEQRA 
(NYCRR 617.4 b (2)); and 
 
WHEREAS, the Riverhead Planning Department Staff, on behalf of the Town 
Board Has completed Part 1 of the Full Environmental Assessment Form (FEAF) dated 
January 31, 2025 as well as Parts 2 and 3 of the SEAF dated April 1, 2025; and

TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
Notice of Adoption 
 
 PLEASE TAKE NOTICE, that the Town Board of the Town of Riverhead, adopted 
a Local Law to Amend Chapter 301 Zoning and Land Development, Part 3 Supplementary 
Use Regulations, Article LIID Battery Energy Storage Systems, §301-283.31 Requirements 
for Tier 2 battery energy storage systems. The intent of the proposed legislation is to 
implement recommendations of the 2024 Comprehensive Plan Update to remove references 
to the Industrial A and Industrial C Zoning Use Districts and include the Calverton Industrial 
and Light Industrial Zoning Use Districts. 
A copy of the entire text of the adopted local law and the provisions of the existing 
law to be amended may be reviewed at the Office of the Town Clerk, 4 W Second Street, 
Riverhead, New York 11901, between the hours of 8:30 a.m. and 4:30 p.m., Monday 
through Friday and can be accessed on the Town of Riverhead website at: 
www.townofriverheadny.gov under the Agenda and Min utes for the April 1, 2025  Town 
Board Meeting.  
Dated:  Riverhead, New York 
   April 1, 2025 
 
 
BY ORDER OF THE TOWN BOARD 
OF THE TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
JAMES M. WOOTEN, TOWN CLERK

Instructions for Completing Part 1 
Part 1 is to be completed by the applicant or project sponsor.  Responses become part of the application for approval or funding, 
are subject to public review, and may be subject to further verification. 
Complete Part 1 based on information currently available.  If additional research or investigation would be needed to fully respond to 
any item, please answer as thoroughly as possible based on current information; indicate whether missing information does not exist, 
or is not reasonably available to the sponsor; and, when possible, generally describe work or studies which would be necessary to 
update or fully develop that information. 
Applicants/sponsors must complete all items in Sections A & B.  In Sections C, D & E, most items contain an initial question that 
must be answered either “Yes” or “No”. If the answer to the initial question is “Yes”, complete the sub-questions that follow.  If the 
answer to the initial question is “No”, proceed to the next question. Section F allows the project sponsor to identify and attach any 
additional information.  Section G requires the name and signature of the applicant or project sponsor to verify that the information 
contained in Part 1is accurate and complete.

Full Environmental Assessment Form 
Part 2 - Identification of Potential Project Impacts 
Part 2 is to be completed by the lead agency.  Part 2 is designed to help the lead agency inventory all potential resources that could 
be affected by a proposed project or action.  We recognize that the lead agency=s reviewer(s) will not necessarily be environmental 
professionals.  So, the questions are designed to walk a reviewer through the assessment process by providing a series of questions that 
can be answered using the information found in Part 1.  To further assist the lead agency in completing Part 2, the form identifies the 
most relevant questions in Part 1 that will provide the information needed to answer the Part 2 question.  When Part 2 is completed, the 
lead agency will have identified the relevant environmental areas that may be impacted by the proposed activity.   
If the lead agency is a state agency and the action is in any Coastal Area, complete the Coastal Assessment Form before proceeding 
with this assessment. 
Tips for completing Part 2: 
• Review all of the information provided in Part 1.
• Review any application, maps, supporting materials and the Full EAF Workbook.
• Answer each of the 18 questions in Part 2.
• If you answer “Yes” to a numbered question, please complete all the questions that follow in that section.
• If you answer “No” to a numbered question, move on to the next numbered question.
• Check appropriate column to indicate the anticipated size of the impact.
• Proposed projects that would exceed a numeric threshold contained in a question should result in the reviewing agency
checking the box “Moderate to large impact may occur.”
• The reviewer is not expected to be an expert in environmental analysis.
• If you are not sure or undecided about the size of an impact, it may help to review the sub-questions for the general
question and consult the workbook.
• When answering a question consider all components of the proposed activity, that is, the Awhole action@.
• Consider the possibility for long-term and cumulative impacts as well as direct impacts.
• Answer the question in a reasonable manner considering the scale and context of the project.

Full Environmental Assessment Form 
Part 3 - Evaluation of the Magnitude and Importance of Project Impacts 
and  
Determination of Significance 
Part 3 provides the reasons in support of the determination of significance.  The lead agency must complete Part 3 for every question 
in Part 2 where the impact has been identified as potentially moderate to large or where there is a need to explain why a particular 
element of the proposed action will not, or may, result in a significant adverse environmental impact. 
Based on the analysis in Part 
3, the lead agency must decide whether to require an environmental impact statement to further assess 
the proposed action or whether available information is sufficient for the lead agency to conclude that the proposed action will not 
have a significant adverse environmental impact.  By completing the certification on the next page, the lead agency can complete its 
determination of significance. 
Reasons Supporting This Determination: 
To com
plete this section: 
• Identify the impact based on the Part 2 responses and describe its magnitude.  Magnitude considers factors such as severity,
size or extent of an impact.
• Assess th
e importance of the impact.  Importance relates to the geographic scope, duration, probability of the impact
occurring, number of people affected by the impact and any additional environmental consequences if the impact were to
occur.
• The as
sessment should take into consideration any design element or project changes.
• Repeat this process for each Part 2 question where the impact has been identified as potentially moderate to large or where
there is a need to explain why a particular element of the proposed action will not, or may, result in a significant adverse
environmental impact.
• Provide the reason(s) why the impact may, or will not, result in a significant adverse environmental impact
• For Conditional Negative Declarations identify the specific condition(s) imposed that will modify the proposed action so that
no significant adverse environmental impacts will result.
• Attach additional sheets, as needed.
Determination of Significance - Type 1 and Unlisted Actions 
SEQR Status:    Type 1   Unlisted

Upon review of the information recorded on this EAF, as noted, plus this additional support information 
and consi
dering both the magnitude and importance of each identified potential impact, it is the conclusion of the 
 as lead agency that: 
  A. 
This project will result in no significant adverse impacts on the environment, and, therefore, an environmental impact 
statement need not be prepared.  Accordingly, this negative declaration is issued. 
 B. Alth
ough this project could have a significant adverse impact on the environment, that impact will be avoided or 
substantially mitigated because of the following conditions which will be required by the lead agency: 
There will, therefore, be no significant adverse impacts from the project as conditioned, and, therefore, this conditioned negative 
declaration is issued.  A conditioned negative declaration may be used only for UNLISTED actions (see 6 NYCRR 617.7(d)). 
 C. This Project may result in one or more sig nificant adverse impacts on the environment, and an environmental impact 
statement must be prepared to further assess the impact(s) and possible mitigation and to explore alternatives to avoid or reduce those 
impacts.  Accordingly, this positive declaration is issued.

04.01.2025 ADOPTED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-324 
 
ADOPTS LOCAL LAW TO AMEND CHAPTER 301 ZONING AND LAND 
DEVELOPMENT, PART 2 DISTRICTS, ARTICLE XLI PINE BARRENS OVERLAY 
DISTRICT, § 301-197 A. (8) (A) CLEARING AND OPEN SPACE STANDARDS, 
PURSUANT TO THE RECOMMENDATIONS OF THE 2024 COMPREHENSIVE PLAN 
UPDATE 
 
Councilman Rothwell offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilman Kern 
 
WHEREAS, by Resolution No. 2024 -760 dated September 4, 2024, The Town 
Board of the Town of Riverhea d issued a Findings Statement and adopted the Town of 
Riverhead 2024 Comprehensive Plan Update; and 
 
WHEREAS, by Resolution No. 2025 -196 the Town Clerk was authorized to 
publish and post a public notice to hear all interested persons to consider a local la w to 
Amend Chapter 301 Zoning and Land Development, Part 2 Districts, Article XLI Pine 
Barrens Overlay District, § 301 -197 A. (8) (a) Clearing and Open Space Standards of 
the Code of the Town of Riverhead (“Riverhead Town Code”); and 
 
WHEREAS, a public hea ring was held on the 4 th day of March 2025 at 2:00 
o'clock p.m. at the Riverhead Town Hall, 4 W Second Street Riverhead, New York, the 
date, time and place specified in said public notice, and all persons wishing to be heard 
were heard, with said hearing closed with a 10-day written comment period; and 
 
WHEREAS, by letter dated March 25, 2025 the Suffolk County Planning 
Commission (SCPC) provided the following Comments:  
  
“Pursuant to the requirements of Sections A 14 -14 to A 14 -25 of the Suffolk 
County Ad ministrative Code, the above referenced application which has been 
submitted to the Suffolk County Planning Commission is considered to be a 
matter for local determination as there is no apparent significant county -wide or 
inter-community impact(s). A deci sion of local determination should not be 
construed as either an approval or disapproval;” and 
 
WHEREAS, at this time the Town Board desires to implement the 
recommendations of the 2024 Comprehensive Plan Update; and  
 
WHEREAS, the proposed amendments are considered an Unlisted Action 
pursuant 6NYCRR Part 617 (SEQRA) and Chapter 225 of the Riverhead Town Code; 
and 
 
WHEREAS, the Riverhead Planning Department Staff, on behalf of the Town 
Board Has completed Part 1 of the Short Environmental Assessment Form (S EAF) 
dated January 31, 2025 as well as Parts 2 and 3 of the SEAF dated April 1, 2025; and 
9.45
Packet Pg. 388
 
RESOLVED, that the Riverhead Town Board hereby assumes Lead Agency and 
issues a Negative Declaration pursuant to SEQRA, for the Local Law to amend Chapter 
301 Zoning and Land Development, Part 2 Districts, Article XLI Pine Barrens Overlay 
District, § 301 -197 A. (8) (a) Clearing and Open Space Standards of the Code of the 
Town of Riverhead (“Riverhead Town Code”) as the proposed action is not likely to 
result in any significant adverse environmental impacts; and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that the local law to Amend Chapter 301 Zoning and Land 
Development, Part 2 Districts, Article XLI Pine Barrens Overlay District, § 301-197 A. (8) 
(a) Clearing and Open Space Standards of the Code of the Town of Riverhead 
(“Riverhead Town Code”) is hereby adopted as specified in the attached notice of 
adoption; and be it further 
 
 RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk be and is hereby directed to forward a copy of 
this resolution to Planning Depa rtment and the Office of the Town Attorney; and be it 
further 
 
RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of 
this resolution from the electronic storage device and, if needed, a certified copy of 
same may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk.   
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Kenneth Rothwell, Councilman 
SECONDER: Robert Kern, Councilman

TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
Notice of Adoption 
 
 PLEASE TAKE NOTICE, that the Town Board of the Town of Riverhead, adopted 
a Local Law to Amend Chapter 301 Zoning and Land Development, Part 2 Districts, Article 
XLI Pine Barrens Overlay District, §301-197 A. (8)(a) Development within Compatible Growth 
Area Clearing and Open Space Standards . The intent of the proposed legislation is to 
implement recommendations of the 2024 Comprehensive Plan Update to remove references 
to the Industrial A, and C Zoning Use Districts and include Calverton Industrial and Light 
Industrial Zoning Use Districts.  
A copy of the entire text of the adopted local law and the provisions of the existing 
law to be amended may be reviewed at the Office of the Town Clerk, 4 W Second Street, 
Riverhead, New York 11901, between the hours of 8:30 a.m. and 4:30 p.m., Monday 
through Friday and can be accessed on the Town of Riverhead website at: 
www.townofriverheadny.gov under the Agenda and Minutes f or the April 1, 2025  Town 
Board Meeting.  
Dated:  Riverhead, New York 
   April 1, 2025  
 
 
BY ORDER OF THE TOWN BOARD 
OF THE TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
JAMES M. WOOTEN, TOWN CLERK

§ 301-197. Development within Compatible Growth Area.  
A. Development within the Compatible Growth Area (CGA) shall comply with the following 
standards: 
(8) Clearing and open space standards 
(a) The proposed disturbance to natural vegetation and minimum open space 
requirements shall be based zoning as of June 28, 1995 or current zoning, 
whichever is more protective of the environment, by minimizing clearance or 
maximizing open space, and shall exclude those lands within EPCAL, and s hall 
conform to the following standards:

For every question in Part 2 that was answered “moderate to large impact may occur”, or if there is a need to explain why a 
particular element of the proposed action may or will not result in a significant adverse environmental impact, please 
complete Part 3. Part 3 should, in sufficient detail, identify the impact, including any measures or design elements that 
have been included by the project sponsor to avoid or reduce impacts.  Part 3 should also explain how the lead agency 
determined that the impact may or will not be significant. Each potential impact should be assessed considering its setting, 
probability of occurring, duration, irreversibility, geographic scope and magnitude.  Also consider the potential for short-
term, long-term and cumulative impacts. 
Check this box if you have determined, based on the information and analysis above, and any supporting documentation,  
that the  proposed  action  may  result in one or more potentially large or significant adverse impacts and an 
environmental impact statement is required. 
Check this box if you have determined, based on the information and analysis above, and any supporting documentation, 
that the proposed action will not result in any significant adverse environmental impacts.

04.01.2025 ADOPTED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-325 
 
ADOPTS LOCAL LAW TO AMEND TOWN CODE ARTICLE LVI: SITE PLAN 
REVIEW 
 
Councilman Kern offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilwoman Merrifield 
 
WHEREAS, by Resolution No. 2025-197, dated February 19, 2025, the Town 
Clerk was authorized to publish and post a public notice to consider a local law to 
amend Riverhead Town Code Article LVI entitled Site Plan Review; and  
 
WHEREAS, a public hearing was held on March 4, 2025 at 2: 00 o’clock p.m. at 
Riverhead Town Hall, 4 W. 2nd Street, Riverhead, NY, the date, time and place specified 
in said public notice, at which time all persons wishing to be heard were afforded an 
opportunity to speak on the matter; and  
 
WHEREAS, the public h earing was closed at the March 4 th, 2025 meeting, with 
the record being left open for the submission of written comments until 4:30 p.m. on 
March 14th, 2025; and  
 
 WHERAS, the proposed code amendment is an Unlisted action pursuant to 
SEQRA, with coordinated review being optional and not recommended; and  
 
 WHEREAS, in a letter dated March 25, 2025, the Suffolk County Planning 
commission provide the following comments: 
 
“Pursuant to the requirements of Sections A14 -14 to A 14 -25 of the Suffolk 
County Admini strative Code, the above referenced application which has been 
submitted to the Suffolk County Planning Commission is considered to be a 
matter for local determination as there is no apparent significant county -wide or 
inter-community impact(s).  A decisio n of local determination should not be 
construed as either an approval or disapproval;” and 
 
 WHEREAS, the Planning Department has prepared a Short Environmental 
Assessment Form Part 1, dated March 12, 2025, as well as SEAF Parts 2 and 3, dated 
March 26, 2025.  Now, therefore be it 
 
 RESOLVED¸ that the Riverhead Town Board hereby issues a Negative 
Declaration pursuant to SEQRA, as the proposed code amendment is not expected to 
have a significant negative environmental impact; and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that the local law to Amend Town Code Article LVI entitled Site 
Plan Review,  hereby adopted as specified in the attached notice of adoption; and be it 
further 
 
9.46
Packet Pg. 398
 RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk be and is hereby directed to forward a copy of 
this resolution to Planning Department and the Office of the Town Attorney; and be it 
further 
  
RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of 
this resolution from the electronic storage device and, if needed, a certified copy of 
same may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk.    
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Robert Kern, Councilman

AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

§ 301-305 § 301-305 
Downloaded from https://ecode360.com/RI0508 on 2024-08-09 
 
 
§ 301-305. Application procedure; fees. [Amended 12-2-2003 by L.L. No. 26-2003; 
4-19-2005 by L.L. No. 10-2005; 4-19-2005 by L.L. No. 11-2005; 11-21-2006 by L.L. No. 
48-2006; 11-7-2007 by L.L. No. 33-2007; 12-6-2011 by L.L. No. 24-2011] 
B. Preliminary site plan application. 
(7) Decision on preliminary site plan application. 
(c) Upon written request by the applicant and prior to the expiration set forth in 
§ 301-305B(7)(b) above, the preliminary site plan approval may be extended for 
an additional six -month period of time after due consideration by the reviewing 
board. No more than two (2) six- month extensions shall be granted by the 
reviewing board.  If an ap plicant fails to apply for final site plan review and 
approval within one year of preliminary site plan approval or, to the extent granted 
by the reviewing board,  within the two (2) six-month extension period(s), the 
Planning Department shall deem the site plan application abandoned such that no 
further action shall be taken by the Planning Department and/or  any such other 
board vested with authority to  review, approve or deny a site plan application, 
and, in such event that an application is abandoned, the Planning Department may 
dispose of and discard all documents, submissions and applications related to said 
application. The Town Building and Planning Administrator, or his or her 
designee, or the Chief Building Inspector shall provide writt en notice 30 days 
prior to expiration of the six- month period referenced above to the applicant 
informing said applicant of the Town Building and Planning Administrator's, or 
his or her designee's, or the Chief Building Inspector's  intent to deem the 
application abandoned. The request for an extension of preliminary 
site plan approval shall be accompanied $250.[ Amended 10-2-
2019 by 
L.L. No. 19-2019; 3-22-2023 by L.L. No. 4-2023] 
 
- Underlines represent additions. 
- Strikethroughs represent deletions.

04.01.2025 ADOPTED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-326 
 
GRANTS SPECIAL PERMIT FOR THE RIVERHEAD CHARTER SCHOOL 
PORTABLE TRAILER APPLICATION 5117 SOUND AVE, RIVERHEAD, NY SCTM 
NO. 600-20-4-3 
 
Councilwoman Merrifield offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilwoman Waski 
 
WHEREAS, the Riverhead Town Board is in receipt of a Special Permit 
application, submitted by the Riverhead Charter School, seeking approval to construct 
three (3) temporary trailers, each having a size of 960 sq . ft. (total 2,880 sq. ft.) for the 
purposes of providing additional classroom space and additional faculty/administration 
space; and  
 
WHEREAS, the subject property, identified as SCTM No. 600 -20-4-3, is located 
at 5117 Sound Ave., Riverhead, NY, within t he Agricultural Protection (APZ) zoning use 
district, and is presently improved with a ±4,690 sq. ft. two -story building, and well as a 
single family residence with detached garage and shed; and  
 
 WHEREAS, by Resolution No. 2024-702, dated August 6, 2024, the Town Board 
scheduled a public hearing on the Special Permit application, as required by Town 
Code §301-311; and  
 
 WHEREAS, a public hearing was held before the Town Board on August 20 th, 
2024, at 6:10 p.m., at which time all those wishing to comment on the application were 
afforded an opportunity to do so; and  
 
 WHEREAS¸ the public hearing was closed on August 20 th, 2024, with the record 
being left open for the submission of written comment until 4:30 p.m. on August 30 th, 
2024; and  
 
 WHEREAS, the Town Board has reviewed a site plan, prepared and stamped by 
Dale E. Koch, PE, last dated April 1, 2024, with sheets labeled C -101: Cover Sheet, C -
102: Notes & Legend, C-201: Existing Conditions/Demolition plan; and  
 
 WHEREAS¸ in a memo dated May 1, 2024, t he Fire Marshal’s office had the 
following comments: 
 
1. Please submit a fire marshal plan addressing Chapter 5 of the NYS Fire Code. 
2. NYSFC503.1.1 – Approved fire apparatus access roads shall be provided for 
every facility, buiding, or portion of a building h ereafter constructed or moved into 
or within the jurisdiction.  The fire apparatus access road shall comply with the 
requirements of this section and shell extend to within 150 feet (45,720mm) of all 
portion of the facility and all portions of exterior wal ls of the first story of the 
building as measured by an approved route around the exterior of the building or 
9.47
Packet Pg. 405
facility. 
3. NYSFC503.2.3 – Road surface must be able to support fire apparatus of 82,000 
lbs. 
4. NYSFC503.2.1 – Fire apparatus access roads shall have an unobstructed width 
of not less than 20 feet (6096mm), exclusive of shoulders, except for approved 
security gates in accordance with Section 503.6, and an unobstructed vertical 
clearance of not less than 13 feet 6 inches (4115 mm). 
5. NYSFC503.2.5 – Dead-end fire apparatus access roads in excess of 150 feet 
(45,720 mm) in length shall be provided with an approved area for tuning around 
fire apparatus; and  
 
 WHEREAS, the proposed action is a Type II action pursuant to 6NYCRR Part 
617.5(c)(8), as it involves the construction or expansion of a primary or accessory, non -
residential structure involving less than 4,000 square feet of gross floor area; and  
 
WHEREAS, the Riverhead Town Board has considered the Special Permit 
application, the SEQRA record to date, the merits of the Site Plan application, the report 
and recommendation of the Planning Department, as well as comments received at the 
public hearing; and  
 
WHEREAS, the Riverhead Town Board has considered the criteria for Special 
Permit consideration, as enumerated in Town Code §301-312 A-R.  Now, therefore be it 
 
RESOLVED, that the Riverhead Town Board hereby grants the Special Permit 
for Riverhead Charter School Portable Trailers at 5117 Sound Ave., Riverhead, NY 
SCTM No. 600-20-4-3, and makes the following Special Permit determination: 
 
1. The use will not prevent or substantially impair the reasonable and orderly 
use or reasonable and orderly development of other properties in the 
neighborhood. 
2. The hazards or disadvantages to the neighborhood from the locat ion of such 
use at the property are outweighed by the advantage to be gained either by 
the neighborhood or the Town. 
3. The health, safety, welfare, comfort, convenience and order of the Town will 
not be adversely affected by the authorized use. 
4. Such use will  be in harmony with and promote the general purposes and 
intent of Article LVII of the Town Code; and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that the Special Permit is hereby granted subject to the following 
conditions: 
 
1. There shall be no further expansion of the school  use on the subject property 
beyond the existing school building and three (3) portable trailers which are 
the subject of this immediate application. 
2. Prior to the issuance of Building Permits, the Riverhead Charter School shall 
post a decommissioning bond with the Town Board in an amount sufficient to 
facilitate the removal of the trailers from the site and remediate the site to 
previous existing conditions. 
3. The Riverhead Charter School shall provide periodic updates to the Town 
Board, at such times as requ ested by the Town Board, as to the status of 
development of another school site elsewhere in the Town. 
4. Prior to the issuance of any Building Permits for interior renovations or site 
9.47
Packet Pg. 406
work, the applicant must receive site plan approval from the Riverhead 
Planning Board and satisfy any and all conditions of site plan approval; and 
be it further 
RESOLVED, in accordance with Town Code §301 -309B, the applicant must 
complete construction and being this specially permitted use within one years of the 
date of adoption of this Resolution; and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is hereby authorized to forward a certified copy 
of this resolution to Raymond Ankrum ( rankrum@rcsli.org); the Planning Department; 
the Building Department; and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that all Town Hall departments may obtain a copy of this resolution 
from the electronic storage device, or may request a certified copy of same from the 
Town Clerk.

Packet Pg. 413
Attachment: TOWN CLERK ABSTRACT 03.27.25  (2025-327 : Pays Bills 3/21/25)
 
04.01.2025 ADOPTED 
 
 
TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-328 
 
AUTHORIZE, NUNC PRO TUNC, LEGAL ACTIONS AGAINST THE OWNER, 
CONTINENTAL INDUSTRIAL CENTER, LLC AND ALL TENANTS AND 
OCCUPANTS OF PREMISES LOCATED AT 28 LINCOLN STREET, RIVERHEAD, 
NEW YORK 
 
Councilman Rothwell offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilman Kern 
 
WHEREAS, the Town Board has determined that the property situated at 28 
Lincoln Street, Riverhead, New York, further described as Suffolk County Tax Map # as 
District 0600-126.00-001-047.00, is being used in violation of various sections of the 
Code of the Town of Riverhead.  
 
 NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that Erik C. Howard, Town Attorney for 
the Town of Riverhead, is authorized, nunc pro tunc, to institute legal action in the name 
of the Town of Riverhead against the owners, tenants and occupants of the structure 
and property situated at 28 Lincoln Street, Riverhead, New York, in the Supreme Court 
of the State of New York, to enjoin the illegal use and/or maintenan ce of said property 
and any structures situated upon said premises; and be it further   
 
 RESOLVED, that it is left to the discretion of Erik C. Howard, Town Attorney for 
the Town of Riverhead, whether said cause of action in the Supreme Court of the State 
of New York to enjoin the illegal use and/or maintenance of said property should further 
seek monetary and/or punitive damages and/or civil penalties against the owners, 
tenants and occupants of the structure and property situated at 28 Lincoln Street, 
Riverhead, New York. 
 
THE VOTE 
 
RESULT: ADOPTED [UNANIMOUS] 
MOVER: Kenneth Rothwell, Councilman 
SECONDER: Robert Kern, Councilman 
AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski
